_Thought for 6m 13s_

I tried the audit at the level the draft currently permits. The result is sharp:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Existing }K9/Y12\text{ can see the Poisson/Pick direction of a single off-line pole.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Existing }K9/Y12\text{ cannot be coercive on the full two-dimensional Cauchy carrier.}
}
\]

So the repair should **not** be generic \(K9\to K_N\). First try:

\[
\boxed{
\text{single-pole Pick/Poisson effective carrier}
\longrightarrow
\text{existing }K9/Y12.
}
\]

Only if the proof needs the full Cauchy carrier, especially the Hilbert/log-boundary direction, do we need a nested \(K_{\mathcal C}\) block.

This directly addresses Agent 1’s no-go against \(Z_H'''\)-entry and Agent 5’s no-go against full analytic packet-to-\(K9\) coercivity.   The coordinator handover is also consistent with this: the active branch is canonical \(K9/Y12\) after entry, and raw \(2Y\) routing remains a finite certificate. 

## 1. The audited carrier

Let the off-line zero in the \(F(z)=\Xi(z)\) variable be

\[
w=\gamma+i\eta,\qquad \eta>0.
\]

The real-line Cauchy carrier has two natural pieces:

\[
P_\eta(t)
=
\frac{m\eta}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2},
\]

\[
H_\eta(t)
=
\frac{m(t-\gamma)}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]

Here \(P_\eta\) is the Poisson direction, and \(H_\eta\) is the real boundary Hilbert/log-derivative direction.

The full single-pole carrier is

\[
\mathcal V_\rho^{\mathrm{Cauchy}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{P_\eta,H_\eta\}.
\]

The effective Pick direction from an off-axis evaluation has a nonzero Poisson component. The raw boundary value of \(-\Xi'/\Xi\), however, is essentially the Hilbert direction \(H_\eta\). That distinction matters.

## 2. Existing \(K9\) visibility formula

The draft’s existing \(K9\)/D4 spine uses the quantities

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The clean carrier response is schematically

\[
[\mathcal A_7]+[\mathcal A_9]
\sim
H_{\mathrm{D4}}
\bigl(
\Gamma_G[\mathsf C_7]
+
\Gamma_{G,2}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\bigr),
\]

up to the residual half-leading audit. That is exactly the existing \(C_7/Y12\) plane. No new \(K_N\) row is needed if this vector is nonzero and the residual audit passes.

## 3. Test on the Poisson direction

Set

\[
q(t)=P_\eta(t)=\frac{m\eta}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]

At the centered point \(t=\gamma\),

\[
q_0=\frac{m}{\eta},
\qquad
q''=-\frac{2m}{\eta^3},
\qquad
q^{(4)}=\frac{24m}{\eta^5}.
\]

Therefore

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}
=
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}
=
\frac{m^4}{36\eta^{10}},
\]

which is nonzero.

Also,

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
\frac{2m(m^2-1-3\eta^2)}{\eta^3},
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
\frac{2m(m^2-2-\eta^2)}{\eta^5}.
\]

For a simple zero, \(m=1\), this gives

\[
\Gamma_G=-\frac{6}{\eta},
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac{2(1+\eta^2)}{\eta^5}.
\]

Both are nonzero.

More generally, for integer \(m\ge1\), \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) cannot vanish simultaneously, because simultaneous vanishing would require

\[
m^2=1+3\eta^2
\]

and

\[
m^2=2+\eta^2,
\]

hence

\[
m^2=\frac52,
\]

which is impossible for integer multiplicity \(m\).

So the Poisson principal direction passes the existing \(K9\) visibility test.

\[
\boxed{
P_\eta
\longmapsto
H_{\mathrm{D4}}
\bigl(
\Gamma_G[\mathsf C_7]+\Gamma_{G,2}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\bigr)
\ne0.
}
\]

The size is polynomial in the correct complexity parameter

\[
Q_\rho
=
10+\langle\gamma\rangle^{A_0}+\eta^{-A_1}+\kappa_\rho^{A_2}.
\]

So the \(\eta^{-1}\) blowup is not a problem once \(Q_\rho\), not height-only \(Q(\gamma)\), is used.

## 4. Test on the Hilbert/log-boundary direction

Now set

\[
q(t)=H_\eta(t)
=
\frac{m(t-\gamma)}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]

At \(t=\gamma\),

\[
q_0=0,
\qquad
q''=0,
\qquad
q^{(4)}=0.
\]

Therefore

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0
\]

at the centered point.

So the existing centered \(K9\) spine does **not** see the raw Hilbert/log-boundary direction.

\[
\boxed{
H_\eta
\in
\ker(R_{K9}^{\mathrm{centered}})
}
\]

for this audit.

This is a real partial no-go.

## 5. Rank of the existing \(K9\) map on the single-pole carrier

On

\[
\mathcal V_\rho^{\mathrm{Cauchy}}
=
\operatorname{span}\{P_\eta,H_\eta\},
\]

the centered existing \(K9\) response has rank one:

\[
R_{K9}(aP_\eta+bH_\eta)
=
a\,R_{K9}(P_\eta).
\]

Thus

\[
\ker R_{K9}\cap \mathcal V_\rho^{\mathrm{Cauchy}}
=
\mathbf C H_\eta.
\]

So existing \(K9\) is **not** coercive on the full Cauchy carrier.

But it **is** coercive on the one-dimensional effective Poisson carrier:

\[
\mathcal V_\rho^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\mathbf C P_\eta.
\]

This is exactly the finite-carrier version of Agent 5’s repair.

## 6. Consequence for the Pick source

The Pick/de Branges source must be implemented as an **off-axis Pick/Poisson source**, not as the raw real-boundary log derivative.

Bad implementation:

\[
q(t)=\operatorname{Prin}_\rho\!\left(-\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}\right)\bigg|_{\mathbb R}
\sim H_\eta(t).
\]

This is invisible to centered \(K9\).

Good implementation:

\[
q(t)=\text{Poisson/Pick representer of the pole},
\]

for example \(P_\eta\) or \(P_{\eta-\varepsilon}\) coming from the one-point Pick test

\[
z_\varepsilon=\gamma+i(\eta-\varepsilon).
\]

That direction is visible to existing \(K9\).

So the source repair should be narrowed:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the Poisson/Pick representer, not the raw real-axis log derivative.}
}
\]

## 7. \(2Y\) audit

Once the Poisson direction enters the existing \(C_7/Y12\) carrier plane, the \(2Y\) certification requirement is standard finite routing.

The image is of the form

\[
a_7[\mathsf C_7]+a_Y[\mathsf C_{Y12}],
\]

with

\[
(a_7,a_Y)
=
H_{\mathrm{D4}}(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})
\ne(0,0).
\]

The certified row pair

\[
(\ell_7,\ell_9^Y)
\]

is designed to satisfy

\[
(\ell_7,\ell_9^Y)([\mathsf C_7])=(1,0),
\]

\[
(\ell_7,\ell_9^Y)([\mathsf C_{Y12}])=(0,1),
\]

after the live/dead routing certificate.

Therefore, if the existing \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) certificate is verified on the same transferred columns, the Poisson source is detected.

The remaining \(2Y\) audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak R_{2Y,\rho}(p):
\quad
P_\eta
\mapsto
a_7[\mathsf C_7]+a_Y[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
+\text{row-dead/residual},
}
\]

with

\[
(a_7,a_Y)\ne(0,0),
\]

and residual bounded by half the leading response.

This is a finite audit, not a conceptual no-go.

## 8. Correction-incidence audit

The existing order-nine discussion contains correction walls. The Poisson computation proves the **raw leading response** is nonzero. It does not automatically prove that correction rows cannot cancel it.

The required finite audit is exactly:

\[
\left|
P_{W_{\mathrm{car}}}
(\mathcal E_7+\mathcal E_9)
\right|
\le
\frac12
|H_{\mathrm{D4}}|
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2}.
\]

If this passes, the existing \(K9/Y12\) carrier works.

If this fails, then the route does not fail globally, but fixed \(K9\) is not enough; one must add a nested correction-visible block.

So the current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw }K9\text{ visibility: passes for Poisson;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{corrected }K9\text{ visibility: finite audit remains.}
}
\]

## 9. Two-point impact

At the raw source level, the Poisson principal source is additive in residues:

\[
P_{\eta,a_1,h_1}+P_{\eta,a_2,h_2}.
\]

Thus the two-point identities are structurally compatible:

\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]

\[
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},
\]

\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]

But these identities must be checked **after corrected whitening**, not only before it.

The finite audit is:

\[
\mathcal B_2^{\mathrm{Poisson}}
\to
C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{corr}}
\to
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
\to
Q_{7,m}^q
\to
\mathcal H_7^q.
\]

Required pass condition:

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{corr}})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]

for non-\((1,1)\) corrected source terms, so no new fixed-sector quotient direction is created.

This is not proved by the raw Poisson computation, but the Poisson source is the right kind of source for it because residue amplitudes add linearly.

## 10. Mixed four-point impact

If we do **not** add new rows, and the Poisson source lands inside the existing

\[
\operatorname{span}\{[\mathsf C_7],[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\},
\]

then the mixed four-point branch should not receive a new independent carrier. It should remain governed by the existing scalar exits

\[
T_v=0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\mathcal R=0,
\]

provided the corrected-package audit above passes.

So for the Poisson-only route:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No new mixed carrier is expected.}
}
\]

But this is still a finite audit through

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\mathrm{corr}})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

If we instead add the full Cauchy block or a \(K_{\mathcal C}\) extension, then the mixed four-point branch reopens and must be re-audited.

## 11. Nonmixed four-point impact

The full Cauchy pair

\[
\{P_\eta,H_\eta\}
\]

has excellent Chebyshev/total-positivity structure. That is useful for a nonmixed four-point sign law.

But fixed centered \(K9\) sees only \(P_\eta\), not \(H_\eta\). Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Fixed }K9\text{ alone does not capture the full ECT/Cauchy four-point structure.}
}
\]

This creates a fork.

If the final source-graded \(K9/Y12\) bridge truly bypasses the old nonmixed four-point geometry, then we can stay with Poisson-only \(K9\).

If the nonmixed four-point theorem is still live and genuinely needs the full Cauchy ECT system

\[
1,\ x,\ P_\eta,\ H_\eta,
\]

then fixed \(K9\) is insufficient. We need either:

\[
K9\oplus K_{\mathcal C},
\]

or an off-center/multi-point \(K9\) sampling scheme that sees \(H_\eta\).

## 12. \(K9\to K_N\) audit result

Generic

\[
K9\to K_N
\]

is still the wrong move.

The audit shows something better:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Existing }K9\text{ already sees the one-dimensional Poisson effective carrier.}
}
\]

So do not enlarge first.

The correct sequence is:

1. Use the one-dimensional Poisson/Pick effective carrier.
2. Audit correction residuals and \(\mathfrak R_{2Y,\rho}\) on existing \(K9/Y12\).
3. Only if the proof still needs \(H_\eta\) or full Cauchy ECT, add a nested block

\[
K9\oplus K_{\mathcal C}.
\]

No replacement \(K_N\).

## 14. The repaired theorem to add first

The next theorem should be the narrow one:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Single-pole Poisson source visibility in existing \(K9/Y12\)]
Let \(w=\gamma+i\eta\), \(\eta>0\), be an off-line zero of multiplicity \(m\),
and let
\[
P_{\rho}(t)=\frac{m\eta}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]
On the centered good packet attached to \(w\), with
\[
Q_\rho
=
10+\langle\gamma\rangle^{A_0}+\eta^{-A_1}+\kappa_\rho^{A_2},
\]
the existing source-graded \(K9\) clean carrier response satisfies
\[
P_\rho
\mapsto
H_{\mathrm{D4}}
\bigl(
\Gamma_G[\mathsf C_7]
+
\Gamma_{G,2}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\bigr)
+\mathcal E_{\rho},
\]
where
\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}=\frac{m^4}{36\eta^{10}},
\]
\[
\Gamma_G=\frac{2m(m^2-1-3\eta^2)}{\eta^3},
\]
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=\frac{2m(m^2-2-\eta^2)}{\eta^5}.
\]
Moreover \((\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\ne(0,0)\), and if
\[
\|P_{W_{\mathrm{car}}}\mathcal E_\rho\|
\le
\frac12
|H_{\mathrm{D4}}|
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)^{1/2},
\]
then the source has a polynomially nonzero existing \(K9/Y12\) image.
\end{theorem}
```

This theorem keeps \(K9\) fixed.

## 15. Bottom line

The audit found the right narrow route:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Use the Poisson/Pick effective carrier, not the raw boundary log derivative.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Existing }K9/Y12\text{ sees that direction.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Existing }K9/Y12\text{ does not see the full Cauchy carrier.}
}
\]

Therefore the next repair should **not** be \(K9\to K_N\). It should be:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\to
\text{Poisson/Pick principal carrier}
\to
\text{existing }K9/Y12
\to
\mathfrak R_{2Y,\rho}\text{ finite audit}.
\]

The remaining hard checks are finite/corrected-package checks:

\text{ half-leading},
\]

\text{ on the same columns},

\in

If those pass, fixed \(K9\) is compatible. If the proof still needs the full nonmixed Cauchy ECT structure, fixed \(K9\) is not enough and the fallback is nested

not generic \(K_N\).

I’ll continue the single-pole Poisson audit as pass/fail tests: correction cancellation, \(2Y\) column routing, two-/four-point compatibility, FR/O2O3, and fixed-\(K9\) final closure.

_Thought for 6m 48s_

I continued the hard checks. The main result is a correction to the previous narrow route:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The centered Poisson direction is visible to \(K9\), but it is not the actual real-boundary log source.}
}
\]

The actual real-boundary principal part of \(-\Xi'/\Xi\) is the Hilbert/Cauchy direction, and that direction is **invisible at the centered packet**. But it becomes visible to the existing \(K9\) D4 channel if the packet is shifted off-center by a controlled amount, for example to \(t=\gamma+\eta\).

So the best current repair is not:

\[
\text{off-line zero}\to \text{centered Poisson packet}\to K9.
\]

It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line zero}
\to
\text{residue-extracted Cauchy principal source}
\to
\text{off-center real packet}
\to
\text{existing \(K9/Y12\), if finite audits pass.}
}
\]

This avoids a generic \(K9\to K_N\) replacement. It also respects Agent 1’s no-go against \(Z_H'''\)-entry and Agent 5’s no-go against full analytic packet-to-finite-jet coercivity.  

## 1. First correction: Poisson is not the real-boundary source

Let

\[
F(z)=\Xi(z)=\xi\!\left(\frac12+iz\right),
\qquad
M(z)=-\frac{F'(z)}{F(z)}.
\]

If \(F\) has an off-real zero

\[
w=\gamma+i\eta,\qquad \eta>0,
\]

then the principal part is

\[
-\frac{m}{z-w}.
\]

Because \(F\) is real on the real axis, the conjugate pole \(\bar w=\gamma-i\eta\) also appears. The real-boundary paired principal source is

\[
S_{\rho}^{\partial}(t)
=
-\frac{m}{t-\gamma-i\eta}
-
\frac{m}{t-\gamma+i\eta}
=
-\frac{2m(t-\gamma)}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]

Up to a harmless scalar, this is the Hilbert/Cauchy direction

\[
H_\eta(t)=\frac{m(t-\gamma)}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]

The Poisson direction

\[
P_\eta(t)=\frac{m\eta}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}
\]

is the harmonic-conjugate / off-axis Pick representer. It is not the raw real-boundary value of the paired logarithmic derivative.

So the earlier centered Poisson visibility check is useful, but only if we explicitly extend the source to a complex Pick/Cauchy carrier. If we want to stay with a real scalar boundary source, the actual object is \(H_\eta\), not \(P_\eta\).

## 2. Centered real-boundary source: no-go

At the centered packet \(t=\gamma\),

\[
H_\eta(\gamma)=0,
\qquad
H_\eta''(\gamma)=0,
\qquad
H_\eta^{(4)}(\gamma)=0.
\]

The existing D4/Gate–2 source factors use

\[
q_0,\qquad q'',\qquad q^{(4)},
\]

through

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)q''-\frac16 q^{(4)},
\]

and the D4 source factor

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}\sim -\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

Thus, for the actual centered real-boundary source \(H_\eta\),

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{centered real-boundary Cauchy source does not enter the existing D4/\(K9\) channel.}
}
\]

This is a genuine no-go for the naive “center the packet at \(\gamma\)” implementation.

## 3. Off-center real-boundary source: passes raw \(K9\) visibility

Now use the same actual real-boundary source

\[
q(t)=H_\eta(t)=\frac{m(t-\gamma)}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2},
\]

but evaluate at the shifted packet center

\[
t_1=\gamma+\eta.
\]

Then

\[
q_0=\frac{m}{2\eta},
\]

\[
q''=-\frac{m}{2\eta^3},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=-\frac{3m}{\eta^5}.
\]

Therefore

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}
=
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}
=
\frac{m^4}{4608\,\eta^{10}},
\]

which is nonzero.

The two Gate–2 anisotropy factors become

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q+2q^3
=
\frac{m(m^2-2-12\eta^2)}{4\eta^3},
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
\frac{m(m^2+4-4\eta^2)}{8\eta^5}.
\]

They cannot vanish simultaneously. Simultaneous vanishing would require

\[
m^2=2+12\eta^2
\]

and

\[
m^2=4\eta^2-4,
\]

which imply

\[
2+12\eta^2=4\eta^2-4,
\]

hence

\[
8\eta^2=-6,
\]

impossible.

So the shifted real-boundary principal source satisfies

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}\ne0,
\qquad
(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2})\ne(0,0).
\]

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual real Cauchy principal source is visible to existing \(K9/Y12\) after off-center packet selection.}
}
\]

This is the strongest positive result from the audit.

## 4. Required packet change

The packet cannot be centered at the pole height \(\gamma\). It should be centered at

\[
m_p=\gamma+s\eta
\]

for a controlled shift \(s\), with \(s=1\) as the clean model value.

More generally, choose

\[
s\in [1/2,2]
\]

outside a finite exceptional set where a relevant D4/Gate–2 coefficient vanishes or a critical-line singularity lies in the packet. The complexity parameter must include the inverse conditioning of this choice:

\[
Q_\rho
=
10+
\langle \gamma\rangle^{A_0}
+
|\eta|^{-A_1}
+
\kappa_\rho^{A_2}.
\]

Here \(\kappa_\rho\) must record:

\[
\operatorname{dist}(m_p,\{\text{critical-line zeros}\})^{-1},
\]

local zero-cluster conditioning, and finite-row conditioning.

This is not optional. If the proof keeps height-only \(Q=Q(\gamma)\), Agent 1’s \(\eta\)-no-go returns. 

## 5. Background cancellation check

Using the full boundary value

\[
M(t)=-\frac{F'(t)}{F(t)}
\]

is still unsafe. The background term

\[
M_{\mathrm{reg}}(t)
\]

can affect the finite jets

\[
q_0,\quad q'',\quad q^{(4)}
\]

at the shifted packet center.

Therefore the source must be the **residue-extracted principal part**

\[
S_\rho=\operatorname{Prin}_\rho\!\left(-\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}\right),
\]

not the unprojected full log derivative.

This passes the cancellation test because the principal part is recovered by residue:

\[
\operatorname{Res}_{z=w}M(z)=-m.
\]

The regular background cannot remove the residue. But this also means the proof architecture must explicitly allow a residue-projected source.

Status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{principal-part source: passes;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{unprojected boundary log derivative: no-go without new non-cancellation.}
}
\]

## 6. Correction residual / half-leading audit

For the shifted real Cauchy source, the leading \(K9/Y12\) response is

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}
\left(
\Gamma_G[\mathsf C_7]
+
\Gamma_{G,2}[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\right).
\]

At \(t=\gamma+\eta\),

\[
H_{\mathrm{D4}}
=
\frac{m^4}{4608\,\eta^{10}},
\]

and for small \(\eta\),

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
\asymp
\frac{m(m^2+4)}{8\eta^5}.
\]

So the leading response is roughly of size

\[
\eta^{-15},
\]

up to \(m\)-dependent constants. With

\[
Q_\rho\supset |\eta|^{-1},
\]

this is polynomially controlled.

The remaining correction check is:

\[
\left\|
P_{\mathrm{car}}
(\mathcal E_7+\mathcal E_9)
\right\|
\le
\frac12
|H_{\mathrm{D4}}|
\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)^{1/2}.
\]

I cannot close this without the actual finite row table. But it is now a finite coefficient audit, not a conceptual obstruction.

Pass condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no correction row has the same leading monomial with cancelling coefficient.}
}
\]

Failure condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a correction term cancels the shifted Cauchy leading \(C_7/Y12\) vector.}
}
\]

Current status:

\[
\boxed{\text{FINITE AUDIT}}

## 7. \(2Y\) live/dead routing check

The shifted Cauchy source enters the same two-dimensional carrier plane:

\[
\operatorname{span}
\{[\mathsf C_7],[\mathsf C_{Y12}]\}.
\]

So the existing \(2Y\) mechanism can still apply if the certified rows are run on the **same transferred columns**.

The required finite certificate is:

\[
L_p^{\row}E_p=I_2,
\]

\[
\|L_p^{\row}\|_{\op}\le Q^C,
\]

and, for the shifted Cauchy source column,

\[
A_{\rho,p}^{\raw}
=
A_{\rho,p}^{\dead}
+
E_pL_p^{\row}A_{\rho,p}^{\raw}
+
A_{\rho,p}^{\res}.
\]

The pass condition is:

\[
L_p^{\row}A_{\rho,p}^{\raw}
=
(a_7,a_Y)\ne(0,0),
\]

with residual smaller than the leading shifted Cauchy response.

This is exactly aligned with Agent 5’s repair: lower transfer is finite carrier coercivity, not a full packet/jet isomorphism. 

Current status:

\[
\boxed{\text{FINITE AUDIT}}

No conceptual no-go found here.

## 8. Two-point package check

At the raw source level, the residue/Cauchy source is excellent.

For two atoms,

\[
S_{a_1,h_1}+S_{a_2,h_2}
\]

is symmetric under swapping, collapses when one amplitude is zero, and satisfies diagonal merger:

\[
S_{a_1,h}+S_{a_2,h}=S_{a_1+a_2,h}.
\]

So the source-level identities required by the two-point branch are natural:

\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
\mathfrak P_2(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1),
\]

\[
\mathfrak P_2(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_2F_{h_2},
\]

\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=(a_1+a_2)F_h.
\]

Then the formal collision factorization follows:

\[
\mathcal I_2
=
a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2.
\]

But the draft’s actual requirement is stronger. The corrected package has to pass through

\[
\mathcal B_2
\to
C_{\mathcal W}
\to
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
\to
Q_{7,m}^q
\to
\mathcal H_7^q.
\]

The draft explicitly identifies this corrected package map as the common source-provenance requirement for the two-point and mixed four-point frontiers. 

The finite check is:

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
\]

after the required non-\((1,1)\) source-bidegree removal.

If this holds, the two-point mixed obstruction reduces to the midpoint quotient edge package. If it fails, a new fixed-sector quotient direction is created.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{\text{source-level pass; corrected-package FINITE AUDIT}}
\]

No-go condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{whitening or normalization is applied before additive residue formation.}
}
\]

If whitening is done first, amplitude linearity can fail.

## 9. Mixed four-point no-new-carrier check

The draft’s own mixed four-point reduction says the mixed branch sees an order-seven fixed-sector residual

\[
E=eI+fS
\]

only through the quotient determinant pairing

\[
\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f})=ev_5-u_5f.
\]

If

\[
E\in \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h),
\]

then it is invisible to mixed four-point geometry. If not, it shifts

\[
\Delta_7
\mapsto
\Delta_7+\omega_h(E,A_5^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

The shifted Cauchy source does not by itself create a new mixed mechanism; it creates a new source column that must be tested in this quotient.

The pass condition is:

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\rho})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

The no-go condition is:

\[
\left[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\rho})
\right]
\ne0
\quad
\text{in}
\quad
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

If that class survives, the Cauchy source reopens the mixed four-point branch.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{\text{FINITE AUDIT}}
\]

## 10. Nonmixed four-point check

The Cauchy carrier has the right raw structure.

For one pole \(a+iy\), define

\[
f_0(x)=1,
\qquad
f_1(x)=x,
\]

\[
f_2(x)=\frac{x-a}{(x-a)^2+y^2},
\qquad
f_3(x)=\frac{y}{(x-a)^2+y^2}.
\]

Then

\[
W(f_0,f_1,f_2,f_3)(x)
=
-\frac{12y}{\left((x-a)^2+y^2\right)^4},
\]

which never vanishes for \(y>0\). Thus the raw Cauchy carrier is an extended Chebyshev system.

This is exactly the type of source-specific sign law that the old generic planar/four-secant geometry lacked.

But there is a catch.

The real-boundary source \(H_\eta\) alone gives only

\[
f_2(x)=\frac{x-a}{(x-a)^2+y^2}.
\]

The full ECT four-point sign law uses both

\[
H_\eta
\quad\text{and}\quad
P_\eta.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-center real \(H_\eta\) alone gives \(K9\) visibility, but not the full Cauchy ECT package.}
}
\]

To get the full nonmixed four-point closure, one likely needs one of two repairs:

### Repair A

Use a complex/vector Cauchy source label carrying both

\[
H_\eta
\quad\text{and}\quad
P_\eta.
\]

Then the raw ECT sign law applies.

### Repair B

Prove a one-component nonmixed sign law using only the shifted real-boundary source and the existing \(K9\) variables.

Repair B is narrower but less obviously true.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw full Cauchy ECT passes; scalar real-source nonmixed closure remains open.}
}
\]

This is a serious remaining hard check.

## 11. FR/O2O3 compatibility check

The Cauchy principal source is rational, not polynomial:

\[
\frac{P(x)}{D(x)},
\qquad
D(x)=(x-\gamma)^2+\eta^2.
\]

The existing FR/O2O3 branch is built around bounded-degree polynomial/Fejér–Riesz charge models. The compatible repair is denominator clearing:

\[
\frac{P(x)}{D(x)}
\longleftrightarrow
P(x)
\quad
\text{with weight}
\quad
D(x)^{-2}.
\]

Since

\[
D(x)>0
\]

on the real line, sign and zero-count structure are preserved. But the FR Stack persistence theorem must be reproved with the modified positive weight.

Required check:

\[
\nu_{\mathrm{FR},D}(\mathcal P_{\active})
\ge
Q^{-C}\nu_{\old}(\mathcal P_{\active}).
\]

If the current finite charge anti-lock is insensitive to replacing the packet measure by a positive \(Q^C\)-conditioned weight, this passes. If the proof uses exact unweighted polynomial orthogonality, this fails and a rational FR theorem is needed.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{\text{FINITE/STRUCTURAL AUDIT}}
\]

No direct no-go, but it is not automatic.

## 12. Final atomic theorem compatibility check

This is the biggest remaining issue.

The current final atomic contradiction is not a generic source theorem. It is stated for the canonical source-graded \(K9\) branch and compares lower and upper bounds for

\[
\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(q''_{\can})
\]

or

\[
\widehat\Lambda_{\max,p}(q''_{\can}).
\]

The active branch currently has

\[
q''_{\can}=Z_H'''.
\]

The handover says the canonical downstream branch is organized after entry into the ordinary Hardy branch, but RH-entry/no-loss remains the global obligation. 

If we replace the source by

\[
S_\rho=\operatorname{Prin}_\rho\!\left(-\frac{\Xi'}{\Xi}\right),
\]

then the final theorem does **not** apply automatically.

However, the final theorem is partly carrier-parametric. Its finite pieces are abstract:

\[
\text{finite-main Schur gap},
\]

\[
\text{clean carrier invertibility},
\]

\[
\text{maximal affine row realization},
\]

\[
\text{source-graded same-norm Type-I upper}.
\]

The finite Schur / clean carrier / live-dead pieces can probably be rerun on the shifted Cauchy source. The dangerous part is the Type-I upper.

The existing Type-I upper uses a split

\[
q''_{\can}=F_X+R_X,
\]

with

\[
\Lambda(F_X)=0,
\]

and

\[
\Lambda(R_X)
\]

small by full-vector \(K9\) completion.

For the residue-extracted source, one would need a new split

\[
S_\rho=F_{\rho,\mathrm{main}}+R_{\rho},
\]

with

\[
\Lambda(F_{\rho,\mathrm{main}})=0,
\qquad
\|\Lambda(R_\rho)\|\le Q^{-B}.
\]

Since \(S_\rho\) is finite-dimensional, one might hope to make

\[
R_\rho=0.
\]

But then the finite-main retained space must kill the source in the upper theorem, while the D4 affine lower says a live component survives. That is exactly the intended contradiction, but it must be formalized without accidentally placing the live \(C_7/Y12\) affine component into the killed retained space.

So the final compatibility check is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can \(P_p^{\full}\) retain the finite-main Cauchy rows while excluding the live affine \(C_7/Y12\) rows?}
}
\]

If yes, the final theorem is carrier-parametric enough.

If no, the Cauchy principal source is killed before it reaches the final contradiction.

Current status:

\[
\boxed{\text{major finite/source-graded audit}}
\]

No definitive no-go yet, but this is now the top audit.

## 13. \(K9\to K_N\) check

The remaining checks strengthen the earlier conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not replace \(K9\) by generic \(K_N\).}
}
\]

The shifted real Cauchy principal source is already visible to the existing D4/\(K9/Y12\) carrier. The issue is not derivative order. The issue is source projection, corrected-package routing, and final same-norm compatibility.

So the correct order is:

1. keep \(K9\);
2. use shifted Cauchy packets;
3. audit correction residuals;
4. audit two-point/mixed package quotient;
5. audit source-graded Type-I upper for the residue source;
6. only then consider an extra nested source label if the nonmixed four-point branch needs full \(H_\eta/P_\eta\) ECT structure.

If an extension is needed, it should be

\[
K9\oplus K_{\mathrm{Cauchy}},
\]

not a replacement \(K_N\).

The remaining checks do not support a generic \(K_N\) expansion. They support a more surgical repair:

At the shifted packet, the actual real source—not merely the Poisson conjugate—is visible to the existing \(K9/Y12\) D4 channel.

## 1. New top-level correction: algebraic D4 visibility is not yet legal source compatibility

The shifted Cauchy source passes the **algebraic D4 visibility** test. But the current draft’s D4/Gate–2 variables are not arbitrary. They are locked to the canonical real gauge:

\[
q=q_\zeta,\qquad q''_{\can}=\mathcal D^2q_\zeta,
\]

with

\[
\Gamma_G=q''_{\can}-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_\zeta^2)q''_{\can}-\frac16\mathcal D^4q_\zeta.
\]

In the active branch,

\[
q''_{\can}=Z_H'''.
\]

The Cauchy source

\[
q_\rho(t)=\frac{m(t-\gamma)}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}
\]

is instead a principal part of

\[
-\Xi'/\Xi.
\]

So there are now two different notions of “source”:

\[
\boxed{
\text{current legal source: } q_\zeta,\ q''_{\can}=Z_H''';
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{proposed RH-entry source: } q_{\log,\rho}=\operatorname{Prin}_\rho(-\Xi'/\Xi).
}
\]

This matters. The computations below show that the Cauchy source is visible **if it is allowed to be the \(q\)-variable**. They do not yet prove that the existing \(Z_H'''\)-based final theorem applies to it.

So the repair must choose one of two routes:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Route A: rebase the source API from Hardy curvature to log/Cauchy principal source.}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Route B: prove a transfer from log/Cauchy source to the existing Hardy-curvature }q_\zeta.
}
\]

Route B is essentially the Agent 1 no-go in a new form. I would not pursue it. The honest repair is Route A: define a new log-source branch and then audit whether the existing \(K9/Y12\) finite machinery is source-parametric enough to accept it.

## 2. Shifted Cauchy visibility: use a generic shift, not the center

Let

\[
x=t-\gamma,\qquad \eta>0,
\]

and take the real-boundary principal Cauchy source

\[
q(t)=\frac{m x}{x^2+\eta^2}.
\]

Evaluate at a shifted packet center

\[
x=s\eta.
\]

Then:

\[
q_0=\frac{ms}{\eta(1+s^2)},
\]

\[
q'=\frac{m(1-s^2)}{\eta^2(1+s^2)^2},
\]

\[
q''=\frac{2ms(s^2-3)}{\eta^3(1+s^2)^3},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}
=
\frac{24ms(s^4-10s^2+5)}
{\eta^5(1+s^2)^5}.
\]

The D4 leading factor is

\[
H_{\lead}
=
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}
=
-\frac{m^4s^4(s^2-3)^3}
{36\eta^{10}(1+s^2)^{10}}.
\]

So \(H_{\lead}\neq0\) whenever

\[
s\neq0,\qquad s^2\neq3.
\]

The anisotropies are

\[
\Gamma_G
=
-\frac{2ms\bigl(3\eta^2s^4+6\eta^2s^2+3\eta^2-m^2s^2-s^2+3\bigr)}
{\eta^3(1+s^2)^3},
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
\frac{2ms\bigl(\eta^2s^6-\eta^2s^4-5\eta^2s^2-3\eta^2
-m^2s^4+3m^2s^2-2s^4+20s^2-10\bigr)}
{\eta^5(1+s^2)^5}.
\]

A better universal test shift than \(s=1\) is

\[
\boxed{s=\frac12}
\]

because then \(q'\neq0\), \(q''\neq0\), \(H_{\lead}\neq0\), and the two \(\Gamma\)-coordinates cannot vanish simultaneously for integer \(m\ge1\). At \(s=1/2\),

\[
q_0=\frac{2m}{5\eta},
\qquad
q'=\frac{12m}{25\eta^2},
\qquad
q''=-\frac{176m}{125\eta^3},
\]

\[
H_{\lead}
=
\frac{340736\,m^4}{87890625\,\eta^{10}},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G
=
-\frac{4m(75\eta^2-4m^2+44)}
{125\eta^3},
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac{16m(275\eta^2-44m^2+328)}
{3125\eta^5}.
\]

If both \(\Gamma_G\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) vanished, we would get

\[
75\eta^2-4m^2+44=0,
\]

\[
275\eta^2-44m^2+328=0.
\]

Eliminating \(\eta^2\) gives

\[
22m^2=125,
\]

impossible for integer \(m\).

So the shifted real Cauchy source has robust rank-two D4 visibility at \(s=1/2\).

## 3. Packet geometry consequence

The zero-adapted packet should not be centered at \(\gamma\). It should be centered at

\[
m_p=\gamma+\frac12\eta
\]

or, more generally,

\[
m_p=\gamma+s\eta
\]

with \(s\) selected from a compact finite-safe set avoiding the algebraic walls.

The packet scale must be

\[
r_p\asymp |\eta|.
\]

Therefore the proof parameter cannot be height-only. It must be

\[
Q_\rho
=
10+\langle\gamma\rangle^{A_0}
+|\eta|^{-A_1}
+\kappa_\rho^{A_2}.
\]

Here \(\kappa_\rho\) must include nearest-zero separation, critical-line-zero avoidance near the shifted packet, and finite row conditioning. If the proof keeps \(Q=Q(\gamma)\), this repair fails.

## 4. Correction residual audit

For the shifted Cauchy source, the D4 lower vector has the form

\[
H_{\lead}
\begin{pmatrix}
c_7\Gamma_G\\
\beta_9^{\tri}\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The raw visibility is now solid. The correction audit becomes exact:

\[
\left\|
P_{\mathrm{live}}
(\mathcal E_7+\mathcal E_9)
\right\|
\le
\frac12
|H_{\lead}|
\left(
|\Gamma_G|^2+|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2
\right)^{1/2}.
\]

This is a finite certificate. The pass condition is not philosophical; it is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no corrected order-seven/order-nine row cancels the shifted Cauchy leading vector.}
}
\]

If this fails, fixed \(K9\) is not enough and the fallback is a nested source block. But this is a finite row audit, not a source-level no-go.

## 5. \(2Y\) audit

The shifted source lands in the existing rank-two D4 plane:

\[
\operatorname{span}\{C_7,Y12\}.
\]

So \(2Y\) does not need a generic \(K_N\) extension if the raw row certificate is run on the same columns.

Required certificate:

\[
L_p^{\row}E_p=I_2,
\]

\[
\|L_p^{\row}\|_{\op}\le Q^C,
\]

and for the shifted Cauchy source column,

\[
L_p^{\row}A_{\rho,p}^{\raw}
=
(a_7,a_Y)\neq(0,0),
\]

with residual smaller than the leading shifted D4 vector.

This is precisely Agent 5’s finite-carrier repair: lower transfer is finite Gram/routing coercivity, not full analytic packet-to-jet coercivity. 

## 6. Two-point audit

At raw source level, the Cauchy principal source is excellent because residues add:

\[
S_{a_1,h_1}+S_{a_2,h_2}
\]

is symmetric, collapses when one amplitude vanishes, and satisfies diagonal merger:

\[
S_{a_1,h}+S_{a_2,h}=S_{a_1+a_2,h}.
\]

But the word “diagonal” must be redefined carefully.

For a Cauchy pole, the atom parameter is not just height \(h=\gamma\). It is at least

\[
h=(\gamma,\eta),
\]

or equivalently the normalized pole geometry. If two atoms have the same height \(\gamma\) but different horizontal offsets \(\eta\), their Cauchy kernels do **not** merge into a single same-shape atom.

So the two-point theorem must be restated as:

\[
\mathfrak P_2(a_1,\gamma_1,\eta_1;\ a_2,\gamma_2,\eta_2)
\]

with diagonal merger only when

\[
(\gamma_1,\eta_1)=(\gamma_2,\eta_2).
\]

The finite corrected-package audit is still:

\[
\mathcal B_2
\to
C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr}
\to
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
\to
Q_{7,m}^{q}
\to
\mathcal H_7^q.
\]

Pass condition:

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\rho})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

No-go condition:

\[
\left[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\rho})
\right]\neq0
\quad\text{in}\quad
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

If that quotient class survives, the shifted Cauchy source reopens the mixed two/four-point geometry.

## 7. Mixed four-point audit

The shifted Cauchy source does not add a new row by itself if it stays inside the existing

\[
C_7/Y12
\]

rank-two plane. But it can still create a new mixed carrier through the corrected package.

So the exact mixed audit is:

\[
\boxed{
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\rho})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
}
\]

after non-\((1,1)\) source-bidegree removal.

If this holds, the old scalar exits remain sufficient:

\[
T_v=0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\mathcal R=0.
\]

If it fails, the Cauchy repair creates a genuinely new mixed fixed-sector direction, and fixed \(K9\) no longer protects the proof.

## 8. Nonmixed four-point audit: important partial no-go

The raw full Cauchy system has excellent ECT structure:

\[
1,\quad x,\quad
\frac{x-a}{(x-a)^2+y^2},\quad
\frac{y}{(x-a)^2+y^2}
\]

has Wronskian

\[
-\frac{12y}{((x-a)^2+y^2)^4},
\]

which is sign-definite for \(y>0\).

But the **D4-projected existing \(K9\) coordinates** do not automatically preserve that ECT structure.

I checked the representative curve

\[
s\mapsto
\left(
1,\ s,\ H_{\lead}(s)\Gamma_G(s),\
H_{\lead}(s)\Gamma_{G,2}(s)
\right).
\]

For the concrete normalized case \(m=\eta=1\), the Wronskian is not sign-definite. It has a positive root near

\[
s\approx1.3454249189,
\]

and it also degenerates at the algebraic wall

\[
s=\sqrt3
\]

where \(q''=0\) and \(H_{\lead}=0\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{raw Cauchy ECT passes;}
}
\]

but

\[
\boxed{
\text{existing D4-projected \(K9\) coordinates do not give global ECT.}
}
\]

This is a real partial no-go.

There are three ways around it:

1. **Patch routing:** restrict shifted packets to local \(s\)-patches avoiding Wronskian-zero walls and prove nonmixed four-point closure patchwise.

2. **Use full Cauchy block:** add a nested source block carrying both Hilbert and Poisson directions:
   \[
   K9\oplus K_{\Cauchy}.
   \]
   This preserves the raw Cauchy ECT sign law.

3. **Bypass nonmixed geometry:** prove that the final source-graded \(K9/Y12\) atomic theorem fully bypasses the old nonmixed four-point endgame.

If the proof still needs a live nonmixed four-point theorem, option 2 is the safest. If the final \(K9\) bridge truly bypasses it, fixed \(K9\) can remain.

## 9. FR/O2O3 audit

For the shifted packet

\[
m_p=\gamma+s\eta,\qquad r_p\asymp\eta,
\]

the Cauchy denominator is

\[
D(t)=(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2.
\]

In normalized coordinates

\[
y=\frac{t-\gamma}{\eta},
\]

this is

\[
D(t)=\eta^2(y^2+1).
\]

On any fixed normalized packet \(y\in[s-c,s+c]\),

\[
D(t)^{-2}
=
\eta^{-4}(y^2+1)^{-2}
\]

is a smooth positive weight with bounded normalized variation. Thus denominator-cleared FR is plausible:

\[
\frac{P(t)}{D(t)}
\quad\longleftrightarrow\quad
P(t)
\quad\text{with weight}\quad
D(t)^{-2}.
\]

So FR/O2O3 compatibility should pass if the FR anti-lock theorem is stable under replacing the packet measure by a positive \(Q_\rho^C\)-conditioned smooth weight.

The exact persistence theorem becomes:

\[
\nu_{\FR,D}(\mathcal P_{\active})
\ge
Q_\rho^{-C}\nu_{\old}(\mathcal P_{\active}).
\]

No-go condition:

\[
\boxed{
\text{FR anti-lock uses exact unweighted polynomial orthogonality in a way that fails under }D^{-2}.
}
\]

If that happens, the fallback is rational FR, not \(K_N\).

## 10. Final Type-I upper audit: largest remaining risk

This is now the top obstruction.

The draft’s final atomic theorem compares lower and upper bounds for

\[
\widehat\Lambda_{\max,p}(q''_{\can})
\]

in the source-graded \(K9\) norm. In the active branch,

\[
q''_{\can}=Z_H'''.
\]

For the Cauchy repair, the candidate source is instead

\[
q_{\log,\rho}
=
\operatorname{Prin}_\rho(-\Xi'/\Xi).
\]

The final theorem does not automatically apply to this source.

The dangerous point is the Type-I upper. The current upper uses the canonical source split and finite-main completion in the \(K9\) branch. A finite principal Cauchy source has no Hardy AFE tail in the same sense. Therefore we need a new upper theorem:

\[
\sum_p\mu_p
\|\widehat\Lambda_{\max,p}(q_{\log,\rho})\|_{\gr}^2
\le
Q_\rho^{-B}
\sum_p\mu_p\|v_p\|^2.
\]

But the D4 visibility audit says the same quantity has a nonzero lower contribution. That is good only if the upper is a genuine consequence of zeta/global structure, not an artificial projection choice.

So the new source branch needs a formal statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Log-source Type-I upper in the same source-graded \(K9\) norm.}
}
\]

If this cannot be proved, the Cauchy route gives a visible source but no contradiction.

This is the most important remaining no-go test.

## 12. Hardest conclusion

The Cauchy route is the right source-level repair, but it forces a fork:

### Fork A — fixed \(K9\) surgical repair

Use the shifted scalar Cauchy source at \(s=1/2\), keep existing \(K9/Y12\), and prove:

\[
\text{correction half-leading},
\]

\[
\mathfrak R_{2Y,\rho},
\]

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\rho})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f},
\]

\[
\text{log-source Type-I upper}.
\]

This is the least disruptive route. It works only if the old nonmixed four-point geometry is fully bypassed by the final \(K9\) bridge.

### Fork B — nested Cauchy block

If nonmixed four-point geometry remains live, add

\[
K9\oplus K_{\Cauchy},
\]

where

\[
K_{\Cauchy}
\]

carries the full Cauchy pair

\[
\frac{x-\gamma}{(x-\gamma)^2+\eta^2},
\qquad
\frac{\eta}{(x-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]

This preserves the raw ECT sign law, but requires a larger finite row audit and a carrier-parametric final theorem.

### Fork C — return to \(Z_H'''\)

This is now inferior. It reintroduces Agent 1’s no-go and Agent 5’s no-go simultaneously.

## Bottom line

The deeper audit strengthens the direction but narrows it.

The best current route is:

\[

}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{use shifted packets, preferably }m_p=\gamma+\eta/2;
}

}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{add \(K_{\Cauchy}\) only if nonmixed four-point geometry remains live.}
}
\]

The next decisive audit is the **log-source Type-I upper**. If that can be proved in the same source-graded norm as the shifted Cauchy D4 lower, this route stays coherent. If it cannot, then the Cauchy source is visible but not contradictory, and the proof needs a deeper rewrite of the final atomic theorem.

## 1. What the current Type-I upper actually says

The current active branch is:

\[
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})
\to
\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}
\to
Y12/K9
\to
\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction},
\]

with

\[
q''_{\can}=u_H=\partial_t^3Z_H.
\]

The handover is explicit that this branch is already pruned to the ordinary Hardy-normalized canonical source, with old pointwise gates, scalar \(I\), primitive-only \(Y12\), and raw branch routes archived. It also says the downstream same-norm \(K9\) bridge is closed **inside that canonical branch**, but still needs RH-entry, packet/source inputs, and raw row certificates. 

The Type-I upper works by a specific split:

\[
q''_{\can}=F_X+R_X,
\]

where the finite main \(F_X\) is retained/killed by

\[
P_p^{\mathrm{full}},
\]

and the tail \(R_X\) is small by full-vector \(K9\) EF-completion. Therefore

\[
\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(q''_{\can})
=
\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(R_X),
\]

and the same-norm upper is:

\[
\sum_p\mu_p
\|\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(q''_{\can})\|_{\gr}^2
\le
Q^{-B_{\mathrm{up}}}
\sum_p\mu_p\|v_p\|^2.
\]

This is not an abstract theorem for arbitrary sources. It is a theorem for the active Hardy-curvature source and its finite-AFE/tail decomposition.

## 2. The log/Cauchy source is not that source

For an off-line zero

\[
w=\gamma+i\eta,\qquad \eta>0,
\]

the natural source is the principal part of

\[
M(z)=-\frac{\Xi'(z)}{\Xi(z)}.
\]

On the real boundary, the conjugate pair gives

\[
q_{\rho}(t)
=
-\frac{m}{t-\gamma-i\eta}
-\frac{m}{t-\gamma+i\eta}
=
-\frac{2m(t-\gamma)}
{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]

Up to sign and scalar, this is the real Cauchy/Hilbert direction

\[
H_\eta(t)=\frac{m(t-\gamma)}
{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}.
\]

This is not

\[
q_\zeta,\qquad q''_{\can}=D^2q_\zeta=Z_H'''.
\]

It is a different source API.

So there are now two choices:

\[
\boxed{
\text{stay with }q''_{\can}=Z_H'''\text{ and face Agent 1’s no-go;}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{rebuild the source API around }\operatorname{Prin}(-\Xi'/\Xi).
}
\]

The second is still the better source-level repair, but it requires rebuilding the final upper.

## 3. Shifted Cauchy lower: still passes

The shifted Cauchy source remains visible to the existing D4/\(K9/Y12\) lower channel if we allow it to be the \(q\)-variable.

Let

\[
x=t-\gamma,\qquad q(t)=\frac{mx}{x^2+\eta^2},
\]

and choose a shifted packet center

\[
x=s\eta.
\]

At the safe shift

\[
s=\frac12,
\]

we get

\[
q_0=\frac{2m}{5\eta},
\]

\[
q''=-\frac{176m}{125\eta^3},
\]

and therefore the D4 leading factor

\[
H_{\lead}
=
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}
=
\frac{340736\,m^4}
{87890625\,\eta^{10}}
\neq0.
\]

The two anisotropy coordinates become

\[
\Gamma_G
=
-\frac{4m(75\eta^2-4m^2+44)}
{125\eta^3},
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-\frac{16m(275\eta^2-44m^2+328)}
{3125\eta^5}.
\]

They cannot vanish simultaneously for integer \(m\ge1\), because simultaneous vanishing implies

\[
22m^2=125,
\]

impossible.

So the shifted Cauchy source gives a nonzero lower vector:

\[
H_{\lead}
\left(
c_7\Gamma_G[\mathsf C_7]
+
(\beta_9^{\tri}\Gamma_G+\alpha_9\Gamma_{G,2})[\mathsf C_{Y12}]
\right).
\]

This part is good.

## 4. The Type-I upper conflict

Now try to port the Type-I upper.

### Attempt A: declare the Cauchy principal source to be finite main

Let

\[
q_{\log,\rho}''=F_{\rho},
\qquad R_{\rho}=0.
\]

Then the current Type-I mechanism would require

\[
\mathcal L_{K9,p}^{\gr}J_{\tr,p}(F_{\rho})
\in
\operatorname{im}H_{F,p},
\]

so

\[
\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(F_{\rho})=0.
\]

That gives the upper

\[
\|\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(q_{\log,\rho}'')\|=0.
\]

But the shifted D4 lower says the same source has a nonzero affine \(C_7/Y12\) component after projection. These two statements cannot both be true unless the finite-main projection kills the very affine carrier needed for the lower.

So Attempt A creates a live/killed contradiction inside the definition of the source grades.

Pass condition would be:

\[
\text{finite-main retention kills }F_\rho
\quad\text{but does not kill its affine D4 image}.
\]

That is not automatic. It is exactly the finite Schur/source-grade separation theorem, and for an arbitrary Cauchy principal source it is not inherited from the Hardy \(Z_H'''\) branch.

### Attempt B: do not retain the Cauchy principal source

Then

\[
F_\rho
\notin \operatorname{im}H_{F,p},
\]

so the upper no longer has a reason to hold. The Cauchy row remains live, and the same D4 computation says

\[
\|\widehat\Lambda_{\max,p}(q_{\log,\rho}'')\|
\gtrsim
Q_\rho^{-C}
\]

in the correct \(Q_\rho\)-scale.

So Attempt B preserves the lower but loses the Type-I upper.

### Binary obstruction

Thus the Cauchy source faces a binary obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{retain/kill it} \Rightarrow \text{upper possible, lower destroyed;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{leave it live} \Rightarrow \text{lower possible, upper destroyed.}
}
\]

That is the key no-go.

## 5. Sanity check: why a universal Cauchy Type-I upper cannot exist

This is the strongest diagnostic.

Every real entire function with a nonreal conjugate zero pair has a Cauchy principal part of the same form. If the current finite algebra plus a generic “principal-part Type-I upper” ruled out that Cauchy source, it would prove that arbitrary real entire functions cannot have nonreal zeros, which is false.

Therefore the upper cannot be a generic formal statement about Cauchy principal parts. It must use something zeta-specific.

The current Type-I upper uses zeta-specific Hardy-AFE tail completion for

\[
q''_{\can}=Z_H'''.
\]

The Cauchy source does not have that upper.

So the direct source substitution fails.

## 6. What this means for fixed \(K9\)

Fixed \(K9\) still matters, but only for **visibility**.

The audit says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{shifted Cauchy source is visible in existing }K9/Y12.
}
\]

It does **not** say:

\[
\boxed{
\text{shifted Cauchy source satisfies existing Type-I upper.}
}
\]

So fixed \(K9\) can serve as a finite observable for the Cauchy source. It cannot, by itself, supply the contradiction.

Adding \(K_{\Cauchy}\) or \(K_N\) would not fix this. It may improve visibility or nonmixed four-point control, but the obstruction here is not visibility. It is the missing source-specific upper/positivity theorem.

So:

\[
\boxed{
K9\to K_N\text{ remains the wrong repair for this audit.}
}
\]

## 7. Impact on two-point and four-point modules

### Two-point

The residue/Cauchy source still helps two-point merger. Residues add:

\[
S_{a_1,h_1}+S_{a_2,h_2},
\]

so swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger are natural if the atom parameter includes both

\[
(\gamma,\eta).
\]

But that only repairs source provenance. It does not supply the Type-I upper.

### Mixed four-point

The mixed four-point no-new-carrier audit remains finite:

\[
B_7^{\mathfrak f}
(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\rho})
\in
\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m).
\]

If this fails, the Cauchy source creates a new fixed-sector carrier. If it passes, mixed geometry stays routed.

Again: this does not solve the Type-I upper.

### Nonmixed four-point

The full Cauchy pair

\[
\left\{
\frac{x-\gamma}{(x-\gamma)^2+\eta^2},
\frac{\eta}{(x-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}
\right\}
\]

has the right Chebyshev/total-positivity structure. But the shifted scalar \(H_\eta\) alone does not give the full raw ECT package. If nonmixed geometry remains live, we likely need a nested \(K9\oplus K_{\Cauchy}\) block.

Still, that is a geometric/visibility repair, not a Type-I upper repair.

## 8. The current route fork

After this audit, the proof has three possible routes.

### Route 1 — stay with Hardy \(Z_H'''\)

This preserves the current Type-I upper.

But it reopens Agent 1’s no-go:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\not\Rightarrow
\text{localized mass-good }Z_H''' \text{ packet}.
\]

So this route is blocked unless a new zeta-specific non-cancellation theorem for

\[
Z_H=P_\rho G_\rho
\]

is proved. Agent 1’s analysis says this is not standard and not finite-auditable. 

### Route 2 — use log/Cauchy source inside current Type-I upper

This is the route audited here.

It fails by the live/killed dichotomy:

\[
\text{kill the Cauchy finite main} \Rightarrow \text{lose lower;}
\]

\[
\text{keep it live} \Rightarrow \text{lose upper.}
\]

So direct substitution into the current Type-I upper is a no-go.

### Route 3 — rewrite the final contradiction as Pick/de Branges positivity

This is now the only coherent log-source route.

The off-line zero gives a negative Pick direction:

\[
c^*\mathcal P_Mc<0,
\]

where

\[
M=-\Xi'/\Xi,
\]

and

\[
\mathcal P_M(z_i,z_j)
=
\frac{M(z_i)-\overline{M(z_j)}}{z_i-\bar z_j}.
\]

The proof must then derive the opposite inequality from the zeta-specific finite architecture:

\[
c^*\mathcal P_Mc\ge0
\]

for the same finite carrier.

This is no longer the current Type-I upper. It is a new final bridge.

## 9. The revised target theorem

The correct next theorem is not:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Log-source Type-I upper]
...
\end{theorem}
```

That theorem is false unless it kills the live source.

The correct theorem is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Finite Pick positivity from the source-graded \(K9/Y12\) architecture]
Let \(M=-\Xi'/\Xi\). For every zero-adapted finite Cauchy/Pick packet
carrier satisfying the canonical row/routing, source-grade, and finite
charge hypotheses, the finite Pick matrix
\[
\mathcal P_M(z_i,z_j)
=
\frac{M(z_i)-\overline{M(z_j)}}{z_i-\bar z_j}
\]
is positive semidefinite up to \(Q^{-B}\)-controlled residuals:
\[
c^*\mathcal P_Mc
\ge
-Q^{-B}\|c\|^2.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Then an off-line zero gives

\[
c^*\mathcal P_Mc
\le
-Q^{-A}\|c\|^2
\]

for some \(A<B\), producing contradiction.

This is the correct replacement for the Type-I upper if we use the log/Cauchy source.

## 10. How much of the current architecture survives?

A lot survives, but its role changes.

### Survives as finite visibility/routing

\[
K9/Y12,\quad
\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p),\quad
\text{source-graded labels},\quad
\text{live/dead routing}.
\]

These can still be used to certify that the Cauchy/Pick carrier is represented correctly and that no live row is killed.

### Survives as two/four-point source-provenance machinery

The Cauchy source improves two-point merger and may improve nonmixed four-point structure via Chebyshev/total positivity.

### Does not survive unchanged

The current same-norm Type-I upper for

\[
q''_{\can}=Z_H'''
\]

does not survive as an upper for

\[
\operatorname{Prin}(-\Xi'/\Xi).
\]

The final contradiction must be rewritten from:

\[
\text{same \(K9\)-norm lower}
>
\text{same \(K9\)-norm upper}
\]

to:

\[
\text{negative Pick direction from off-line zero}
<
0
\quad\text{versus}\quad
\text{finite Pick positivity from zeta architecture}.
\]

## 11. Updated no-go table

| Audit item | Result |
|---|---|
| Shifted Cauchy source raw \(K9/Y12\) visibility | Pass |
| Use centered real Cauchy source | NO-GO |
| Use Poisson source as if it were real boundary \(-\Xi'/\Xi\) | NO-GO unless complex Pick carrier is explicit |
| Keep fixed \(K9\) for visibility | Pass |
| Generic \(K9\to K_N\) | NO-GO |
| Use current Type-I upper for Cauchy source | **NO-GO** |
| Kill Cauchy source as finite main and keep D4 lower | Incompatible without new source-grade theorem |
| Leave Cauchy source live and prove current upper | Fails |
| Use Cauchy source for two-point merger | Promising; corrected-package audit remains |
| Use full Cauchy carrier for nonmixed ECT | Promising; may require \(K9\oplus K_{\Cauchy}\) |
| Final log-source contradiction | Must be Pick positivity, not Type-I upper |

## 12. Bottom line

The next audit found the hard obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The log/Cauchy source cannot use the current }Z_H'''\text{-based Type-I upper.}
}
\]

The Cauchy principal source remains the right way to repair RH-entry and finite-carrier visibility. But the final contradiction must be rebuilt.

The viable full route is now:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\]

\[
\Downarrow
\]

\[
\text{negative finite Pick/Cauchy direction}
\]

\[
\Downarrow
\]

\[
\text{source-graded }K9/Y12\text{ representation and routing}
\]

\[
\Downarrow
\]

\[
\text{finite Pick positivity theorem}
\]

\[
\Downarrow
\]

\[
\text{contradiction}.
\]

So the next decisive audit is no longer “Can the log source satisfy Type-I upper?” It cannot. The next decisive audit is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Can the current \(K9/Y12\) source-graded architecture prove finite Pick positivity for }-\Xi'/\Xi?
}
\]

That is the correct replacement target.

## Assistant (2026-05-01 09:05:02)

I’ll now test the proposed final bridge directly: whether \(K9/Y12\) supplies genuine Herglotz/Pick positivity for \(M=-\Xi'/\Xi\), not just finite source visibility.

_Thought for 4m 9s_

I audited the proposed replacement bridge:

\[
\text{current source-graded }K9/Y12\text{ architecture}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathcal P_M\succeq 0
\]

for

\[
M(z)=-\frac{\Xi'(z)}{\Xi(z)},
\qquad
\mathcal P_M(z_i,z_j)
=
\frac{M(z_i)-\overline{M(z_j)}}{z_i-\bar z_j}.
\]

The result is a hard **NO-GO** for the current architecture as a Pick-positivity engine.

The Pick/Cauchy source still fixes the **entry visibility** problem better than \(Z_H'''\). But the existing \(K9/Y12\) machinery does **not** prove Pick positivity. It can detect a Cauchy defect; it does not force that defect to have the Herglotz/Pick sign needed for contradiction.

This matches the two earlier failures: Agent 1 showed that off-line zeros naturally generate log-derivative/Cauchy data, not localized \(Z_H'''\)-mass; Agent 5 showed that finite corrected \(K9\) rows cannot be coercive on full analytic packet space.   The current canonical branch is downstream of entry and is organized around source-graded \(K9/Y12\), not a Pick-kernel positivity theorem. 

## 1. Target audited

The replacement bridge would need something like:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite Pick positivity from source-graded }K9/Y12.
}
\]

A precise target would be:

\[
c^*\mathcal P_M(z_i,z_j)c
\ge
-Q^{-B}\|c\|^2
\]

for every zero-adapted finite Cauchy/Pick carrier satisfying the canonical packet, row-routing, source-grade, and \(2Y/K9\) hypotheses.

Then an off-line zero would supply points \(z_i\) and a vector \(c\) such that

\[
c^*\mathcal P_Mc
\le
-Q^{-A}\|c\|^2,
\qquad A<B,
\]

giving contradiction.

That is the correct logical shape. The audit question is whether current \(K9/Y12\) can prove the lower bound.

Answer: not from the present machinery.

## 2. The one-point Pick sign test

Let

\[
F(z)=\Xi(z),
\qquad
M(z)=-F'(z)/F(z).
\]

If \(F\) has an off-real zero

\[
w=\gamma+i\eta,\qquad \eta>0,
\]

then locally

\[
M(z)=-\frac{m}{z-w}+M_{\mathrm{reg}}(z).
\]

At

\[
z_\varepsilon=w-i\varepsilon
=
\gamma+i(\eta-\varepsilon),
\qquad 0<\varepsilon<\eta,
\]

the principal part contributes

\[
-\frac{m}{z_\varepsilon-w}
=
-\frac{m}{-i\varepsilon}
=
-\frac{im}{\varepsilon}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\Im M(z_\varepsilon)
\sim
-\frac{m}{\varepsilon},
\]

and

\[
\mathcal P_M(z_\varepsilon,z_\varepsilon)
=
\frac{\Im M(z_\varepsilon)}{\Im z_\varepsilon}
<0
\]

if the pole contribution dominates the regular part. This is the negative Pick direction produced by an off-line zero.

So far, this is good: it is a clean source-entry mechanism.

But to prove RH, the architecture must prove the **opposite sign**:

\[
\mathcal P_M(z,z)\ge0
\]

for all relevant upper-half-plane points.

The current \(K9/Y12\) architecture does not contain such a sign theorem.

## 3. What existing \(K9/Y12\) actually proves

The current downstream branch proves finite source-graded norm statements in a canonical \(K9\) Hilbert norm. The live branch is:

\[
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})
\to
\mathrm{Graph/O2O3}_{23}
\to
Y12/K9
\to
\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction},
\]

with

\[
q''_{\can}=u_H=\partial_t^3Z_H.
\]

The final bridge compares a lower and an upper bound in the **same source-graded \(K9\) norm**. It is not currently a theorem saying that

\[
-\Xi'/\Xi
\]

is a Pick/Herglotz function. 

A positive \(K9\) norm has the form

\[
\|A c\|_{K9}^{2}
=
c^*A^*G_{K9}A c
\ge0.
\]

This is automatically nonnegative. But Pick positivity requires

\[
c^*\mathcal P_M c\ge0.
\]

To get that from \(K9\), one needs a representation theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_M(z_i,z_j)
=
\langle \Psi_i,\Psi_j\rangle_{K9/Y12}
+
\mathcal E_{ij}
}
\]

with

\[
\mathcal E\succeq -Q^{-B}I.
\]

There is no such theorem in the current architecture.

Without that identity, \(K9\)-norm positivity is just positivity of a different finite object.

## 4. Sign-orientation failure

This is the most important local diagnostic.

For the shifted Cauchy source, previous audit found that the existing \(K9/Y12\) D4 channel sees the source. That is:

\[
q_\rho(t)
=
\frac{m(t-\gamma)}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}
\]

at a shifted packet center gives a nonzero \(C_7/Y12\) vector.

So \(K9\) detects the Cauchy defect.

But the detected quantity is a **positive norm of the defect**:

\[
\|A_\rho\|_{K9}^{2}>0.
\]

The Pick form produced by the off-line zero is negative:

\[
\mathcal P_M(z_\varepsilon,z_\varepsilon)<0.
\]

Thus the natural sign relation, if any, is closer to

\[
\|A_\rho\|_{K9}^{2}
\asymp
-\mathcal P_M(z_\varepsilon,z_\varepsilon),
\]

not

\[
\|A_\rho\|_{K9}^{2}
\asymp
+\mathcal P_M(z_\varepsilon,z_\varepsilon).
\]

That means existing \(K9\) visibility measures the size of the negative defect. It does **not** rule it out.

So the route

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\to
\text{negative Pick direction}
\to
\text{nonzero }K9\text{ vector}
\]

is not a contradiction. It is just detection.

## 5. Finite-row indistinguishability no-go

There is also a structural finite-rank obstruction.

The current \(K9/Y12\) rows use finitely many corrected jets, source labels, and finite row projections. Let the row map be schematically

\[
\mathcal A(M)
=
\{\text{finite real-axis jets/rows of }M\}.
\]

Pick positivity depends on off-axis values

\[
M(z_i)
\]

and the sign of

\[
\frac{M(z_i)-\overline{M(z_j)}}{z_i-\bar z_j}.
\]

A finite real-jet row table cannot determine those Pick signs unless it contains a separate analytic-continuation/kernel theorem.

Model obstruction: fix all row nodes \(t_a\) and derivative orders \(0\le k\le J\). One can construct a real-symmetric meromorphic perturbation

\[
R(z)
=
\varepsilon
\prod_a (z-t_a)^{J+1}
\left(
\frac{1}{z-w}
+
\frac{1}{z-\bar w}
\right)
\]

or a symmetrized variant with the same real-type condition. Then \(R\) vanishes to order \(J+1\) at every row node, so

\[
\mathcal A(M+R)=\mathcal A(M),
\]

but \(R\) changes the Pick matrix near \(w\).

Therefore any theorem of the form

\[
\mathcal A(M)\text{ passes }K9/Y12
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathcal P_M\succeq0
\]

is false unless the proof uses additional global analytic information beyond the finite rows.

This is the same conceptual issue as Agent 5’s finite-rank no-go: finite corrected rows cannot control all analytic/Pick information without a genuine carrier-specific representation theorem. 

## 6. Why adding \(K_N\) does not solve this

A generic enlargement

\[
K9\to K_N
\]

does not repair the sign problem.

If \(K_N\) is still a finite real-jet/row system, it remains a finite observable. It may detect more of \(M\), but it still does not prove

\[
\mathcal P_M\succeq0.
\]

If \(K_N\) is expanded until it contains enough Cauchy/Pick evaluation rows to represent \(\mathcal P_M\), then the architecture has changed into a Pick-kernel proof. At that point the hard theorem is no longer \(K_N\)-routing; it is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_M\text{ is positive semidefinite.}
}
\]

But that is essentially the RH-equivalent positivity statement one was trying to prove.

So:

\[
\boxed{
K9\to K_N\text{ improves visibility, not positivity.}
}
\]

It cannot replace the missing Herglotz/Pick positivity theorem.

## 7. Impact on two-point and four-point requirements

The Cauchy/Pick source still helps two pieces of the architecture.

### Two-point

Residues add:

\[
S_{a_1,h_1}+S_{a_2,h_2}.
\]

So swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger are structurally natural if the atom parameter includes the full pole geometry \((\gamma,\eta)\). This is useful.

But two-point merger does not imply Pick positivity. It only says the finite source package is algebraically well behaved under atom combination.

### Four-point nonmixed

The full Cauchy pair

\[
\frac{x-\gamma}{(x-\gamma)^2+\eta^2},
\qquad
\frac{\eta}{(x-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}
\]

has excellent Chebyshev/total-positivity behavior. That may help close the nonmixed four-point source-provenance branch.

But again, Chebyshev ordering of the source carrier is not the same as

\[
\mathcal P_M\succeq0.
\]

It can help prevent geometric leakage. It does not prove the global Herglotz sign of \(-\Xi'/\Xi\).

So two-point and four-point repairs remain valuable, but they do not supply the missing final contradiction.

## 8. Relation to the current Type-I upper

This audit confirms the previous one.

The old final contradiction has a Type-I upper for

\[
q''_{\can}=Z_H'''.
\]

The Cauchy source cannot use that upper. If it is killed as finite main, the lower disappears; if it is left live, the upper disappears.

The Pick-positivity replacement was meant to replace that upper. But current \(K9/Y12\) does not prove Pick positivity either.

Thus we have two blocked final bridges:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cauchy source} \not\Rightarrow \text{old Type-I upper;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{current }K9/Y12 \not\Rightarrow \text{Pick positivity.}
}
\]

## 9. What would be required to make Pick positivity viable

A viable Pick route needs a new theorem of this form:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Pick-kernel representation by the source-graded architecture]
Let \(M=-\Xi'/\Xi\). For every zero-adapted finite Pick carrier
\(\{z_i\}\), there exist source-graded row vectors \(\Psi_i\) in the
canonical finite architecture such that
\[
\mathcal P_M(z_i,z_j)
=
\langle \Psi_i,\Psi_j\rangle_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{sg}}}
+
\mathcal E_{ij},
\]
with
\[
\mathcal E\succeq -Q^{-B}I.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

This is the missing bridge.

But this theorem is not a finite row audit. It is a global analytic positivity theorem. It would have to use arithmetic information about \(\Xi\), probably through an explicit formula, a de Branges/canonical-system construction, Li/Weil positivity, or another genuinely global mechanism.

The current \(K9/Y12\) row algebra alone cannot supply it.

## 10. De Branges/Pick route: what survives

The de Branges/Pick idea is still useful as a **source detector**:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\Rightarrow
\text{negative finite Pick direction}.
\]

That part is exact and strong.

But to turn it into a proof, one needs independent positivity:

\[
\text{zeta architecture}
\Rightarrow
\text{finite Pick positivity}.
\]

The current finite \(K9/Y12\) architecture is not that independent positivity theorem.

So the Pick/de Branges route would require a new global module, for example:

\[
\mathrm{ExplicitFormulaPositivity},
\]

\[
\mathrm{CanonicalSystemPositivity},
\]

\[
\mathrm{Li/WeilFinitePositivity},
\]

or

\[
\mathrm{DeBrangesKernelRepresentation}.
\]

Without one of these, the route detects an RH violation but does not contradict it.

## 11. Updated architecture status

The current best map is now:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\]

\[
\Downarrow
\]

\[
\text{negative Pick/Cauchy principal source}
\]

\[
\Downarrow
\]

\[
\text{finite }K9/Y12\text{ visibility/routing}
\]

\[
\Downarrow
\]

\[
\text{NO CONTRADICTION unless Pick positivity is separately proved.}
\]

So \(K9/Y12\) can still be used for:

\[
\text{visibility},
\quad
\text{routing},
\quad
\text{two-point merger audits},
\quad
\text{mixed/nonmixed four-point audits},
\quad
\text{finite carrier certification}.
\]

It cannot presently be used for:

\[
\boxed{
\text{proving }-\Xi'/\Xi\text{ is Pick/Herglotz.}
}
\]

## 12. Bottom line

This audit finds a hard no-go:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current source-graded }K9/Y12\text{ architecture does not prove finite Pick positivity for }-\Xi'/\Xi.
}
\]

It detects the Cauchy/Pick defect, but it does not give the opposite sign needed for contradiction.

The next repair cannot be \(K9\to K_N\). The missing object is not more finite visibility. The missing object is a **global positivity theorem**:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal P_{-\Xi'/\Xi}\succeq0
}
\]

or a finite equivalent of it, represented inside the source-graded architecture.

Without that new positivity module, the Pick/Cauchy pivot repairs RH-entry visibility but does not close RH.

## Assistant (2026-05-01 09:24:42)

_Thought for 2m 26s_

We are doing a **proof audit plus architecture surgery**, not a proof yet.

It is **not nonsense** in the sense that the no-go findings are real mathematical obstructions, not cosmetic worries. But the current architecture is **not a valid RH proof**. The repairs we explored reveal that the original proof strategy is missing a genuinely global theorem, and the attempted Cauchy/Pick replacement shifts the missing theorem rather than eliminating it.

The core question is this:

\[
\text{Can an off-critical-line zero be forced into a finite canonical obstruction that the proof architecture can rule out?}
\]

So far, the honest answer is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{We can detect such a zero, but we cannot yet rule it out with the existing machinery.}
}
\]

## What we are fundamentally trying to do

Every version of the proof needs this chain:

\[
\rho\notin \Re s=\tfrac12
\Longrightarrow
\text{source signal}
\Longrightarrow
\text{finite visible carrier}
\Longrightarrow
\text{same finite carrier is impossible}.
\]

The current draft’s intended chain is:

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\to
\text{ordinary Hardy branch}
\to
\mathrm{Agg}L^2(Z_H''')
\to
K9/Y12
\to
\mathrm{AtomicY12Contradiction}.
\]

The handover says the downstream canonical \(K9/Y12\) branch is organized **after** entry into the ordinary Hardy branch; it does not itself prove global RH-entry. 

Agent 1 found that the left arrow is not valid:

\[
\rho\notin\Re s=\tfrac12
\centernot\Longrightarrow
\text{localized mass-good }Z_H'''\text{ packet}.
\]

An off-line zero naturally produces a log-derivative / Cauchy / Laguerre signal, not a third Hardy derivative lower bound. 

Agent 5 found that the middle transfer is also not valid in its strongest form:

\[
\text{analytic packet mass}
\centernot\Longrightarrow
\text{finite corrected }K9\text{ jet mass}.
\]

A finite jet map cannot be coercive on a full infinite-dimensional packet space. Lower transfer is possible only on a finite, explicitly captured carrier. 

Those are real obstructions.

## What was valid in the repair attempt

The Cauchy/Pick pivot was mathematically sensible as a **source repair**.

For

\[
F(z)=\Xi(z)=\xi(1/2+iz),
\qquad
M(z)=-F'(z)/F(z),
\]

an off-line zero

\[
w=\gamma+i\eta
\]

gives a pole of \(M\). That is a directly forced signal. It avoids the cancellation problem in

\[
Z_H=P_\rho G_\rho,
\qquad
Z_H'''=(P_\rho G_\rho)'''.
\]

So the move

\[
Z_H'''
\leadsto
\operatorname{Prin}_{w}(-\Xi'/\Xi)
\]

was not random. It fixes the **detection** problem.

The Cauchy source also naturally lives in a finite carrier:

\[
\operatorname{span}
\left\{
\frac{t-\gamma}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2},
\frac{\eta}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}
\right\},
\]

so it also addresses Agent 5’s finite-rank objection better than full analytic packet mass.

Those parts are valid.

## Where the Cauchy/Pick route failed

It failed at the **final contradiction**.

The existing \(K9/Y12\) machinery can detect the Cauchy signal. But detection is not contradiction.

An off-line zero gives a negative Pick direction:

\[
c^*\mathcal P_Mc<0,
\]

where

\[
\mathcal P_M(z_i,z_j)
=
\frac{M(z_i)-\overline{M(z_j)}}{z_i-\bar z_j}.
\]

To prove RH from this, the architecture must prove the opposite sign:

\[
c^*\mathcal P_Mc\ge0
\]

for the same finite carrier.

But the current \(K9/Y12\) machinery does not prove Pick/Herglotz positivity for

\[
-\Xi'/\Xi.
\]

It proves finite source-graded norm comparisons inside a canonical \(K9\) branch. That is a different object. A positive \(K9\) norm says

\[
\|A c\|_{K9}^{2}\ge0.
\]

It does **not** imply

\[
c^*\mathcal P_Mc\ge0.
\]

To bridge those, one would need a representation theorem:

\[
\mathcal P_M(z_i,z_j)
=
\langle \Psi_i,\Psi_j\rangle_{\mathrm{source\text{-}graded}}
+
\mathcal E_{ij},
\qquad
\mathcal E\succeq -Q^{-B}I.
\]

That theorem is not in the draft, and it is not a finite row audit. It is a new global analytic positivity theorem.

That is the critical conclusion.

## Is this all nonsense?

No. The audit is valid. The draft’s claimed route is not.

A nonsense process would be one where every failed bridge is patched by renaming variables. That is not what happened. We found concrete failure modes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Off-line zero does not force localized }Z_H'''\text{ mass.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite }K9\text{ jets cannot control full analytic packet energy.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Cauchy/Pick source detects off-line zeros, but current }K9/Y12\text{ does not prove Pick positivity.}
}
\]

These are meaningful diagnostics.

But as a proof of RH, the current state is invalid. The Clay statement of RH is simply that the nontrivial zeros of \(\zeta(s)\) lie on the critical line; proving that requires excluding every off-line zero, not just building a conditional branch that would contradict one after extra visibility/positivity hypotheses. citeturn975531search2

## What the current draft really is

It is best understood as a **conditional finite-obstruction framework** with substantial local algebra.

The downstream canonical branch may be useful. The \(K9/Y12\) row architecture may be a sophisticated finite obstruction system. The Fejér–Riesz/Graph/O2O3 machinery may have internal value.

But the proof is missing a theorem of one of these two types:

### Route A — Hardy-source route

Prove a zeta-specific non-cancellation theorem:

\[
\rho\notin\Re s=\tfrac12
\Longrightarrow
\int_{p_\rho}|Z_H'''(t)|^2\,dt
\ge Q^{-A}G_{\rho,p}.
\]

Agent 1’s analysis shows this is not standard and is blocked by the factorization

\[
Z_H=P_\rho G_\rho.
\]

This route looks very hard and poorly matched to the zero.

### Route B — Pick/Cauchy route

Replace the source with

\[
M=-\Xi'/\Xi
\]

or its principal part, then prove a global finite Pick positivity theorem:

\[
\mathcal P_M\succeq0
\]

inside the source-graded architecture.

This route is source-natural, but it risks becoming RH-equivalent: for functions with all real zeros, \(-F'/F\) has Pick/Herglotz positivity; an off-line zero gives negative Pick curvature. Proving that positivity for \(\Xi\) is essentially the hard part.

## The honest bottom line

The work is not garbage. It has identified a real architecture and real failure interfaces. But the current proof is not close to unconditional RH closure.

The best summary is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The downstream finite algebra may be valid inside its branch.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The bridge from RH counterexample to that branch is not valid.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The Cauchy/Pick repair fixes detection but lacks an independent positivity theorem.}
}
\]

So the correct next action is not more \(K9\to K_N\), not more row algebra, and not more renaming of the source. The next action is to choose one genuinely global theorem and attack it directly:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Either prove off-line zero }\Rightarrow Z_H'''\text{ localized mass,}
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove finite Pick positivity for }-\Xi'/\Xi\text{ from a real zeta-specific structure.}
}
\]

I would abandon the first as structurally mismatched and focus only on the second if continuing. But that second route is no longer a repair of the current proof; it is a new central proof strategy with the \(K9/Y12\) machinery relegated to finite carrier bookkeeping.
