# 2. Insert a “no full packet/jet lower bound” lemma

Place this immediately after Remark `canonical-packet-to-corrected-jet-transfer-discipline` near the final canonical ledger, or near the first place the packet-to-\(K9\) transfer is discussed.

```latex
\begin{lemma}[No full packet-to-\(K9\) lower bound]
\label{lem:no-full-packet-to-K9-lower-bound}
Let \(p\) be a good analytic packet and let
\[
  T_p
  =
  (I-P_p^{\full})
  \mathcal L_{K9,p}^{\gr}J_{\tr,p}
\]
be any corrected \(K9\) jet map using finitely many transition jets and finitely
many labelled row projections.  Then no constants \(C\) and \(Q\) can make
\[
  Q^{-C}\|v\|_{\pkt,J,p}^{2}
  \le
  \|T_pv\|_{\gr}^{2}
\]
hold for every \(v\in H^J(K_p^+)\).

Consequently, all lower packet-to-\(K9\) transfer statements in the proof must
be restricted to a finite certified carrier or to a quotient of such a carrier.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The map \(T_p\) has finite rank because it depends on finitely many transition
jets and finitely many finite row projections.  The analytic packet space
\(H^J(K_p^+)\) is infinite-dimensional.  Hence \(\ker T_p\) is
infinite-dimensional.  Choose nonzero \(v\in\ker T_p\).  Then
\[
  \|T_pv\|_{\gr}=0,
  \qquad
  \|v\|_{\pkt,J,p}>0,
\]
contradicting any lower bound of the displayed form.
\end{proof}
```

This lemma prevents the old anti-heartbreak theorem from reappearing in a false form.

---

# 3. Insert the finite carrier definitions

Place after the no-full-lower-bound lemma.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Hardy-source finite carrier]
\label{def:hardy-source-finite-carrier}
On a good ordinary Hardy-normalized packet \(p\), the Hardy-source finite carrier
is a finite-dimensional subspace
\[
  \mathcal V_{\pkt,p}^{\car}
  =
  \operatorname{span}\{\psi_{p,1},\ldots,\psi_{p,N_p}\}
  \subset H^J(K_p^+)
\]
containing the packet restrictions of the following proof-level objects:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},nosep]
\item the Hardy-differential AFE main pieces for
      \(u_H=\partial_t^3Z_H\);
\item the gamma/theta derivative and log-power pieces appearing in the
      differentiated Hardy AFE;
\item the pre-extraction Fej\'er--Riesz Stack charge pieces used by the
      finite/O2O3 branch;
\item the transition/corrected-jet model pieces used by
      \(\mathcal L_{K9,p}^{\gr}J_{\tr,p}\);
\item the retained labelled affine \(C_7/Y12\) directions.
\end{enumerate}
The effective carrier
\[
  \mathcal V_{\pkt,p}^{\eff}
  \subseteq
  \mathcal V_{\pkt,p}^{\car}
\]
is obtained by removing row-dead directions and declared \(Q^{-B}\)-residual
directions.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Carrier Gram audit]
\label{def:carrier-Gram-audit-K9}
For a certified carrier basis
\[
  \mathcal B_p=\{\psi_{p,1},\ldots,\psi_{p,N_p}\},
\]
define the packet Gram matrix
\[
  G_{\pkt,p}
  =
  \bigl(
  \langle\psi_{p,i},\psi_{p,j}\rangle_{\pkt,J,p}
  \bigr)_{i,j},
\]
the corrected \(K9\) jet matrix
\[
  A_p
  =
  \left[
  \Lambda_p^{\gr,full}\psi_{p,1}\ \cdots\
  \Lambda_p^{\gr,full}\psi_{p,N_p}
  \right],
\]
and the source-graded target Gram matrix \(G_{\jet,p}^{\gr}\).  The carrier
Gram audit is the finite certificate
\[
  A_p^*G_{\jet,p}^{\gr}A_p
  \ge
  Q^{-C_{\gram}}G_{\pkt,p}
  \qquad
  \text{on }\mathcal V_{\pkt,p}^{\eff}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
  \sigma_{\min}
  \left(
  (G_{\jet,p}^{\gr})^{1/2}
  A_p
  G_{\pkt,p}^{-1/2}
  \bigm|_{\mathcal V_{\pkt,p}^{\eff}}
  \right)
  \ge Q^{-C_{\gram}}.
\]
\end{definition}
```

# 4. Insert the carrier-corrected packet-to-\(K9\) theorem

Place after the carrier definitions.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Carrier-corrected packet-to-\(K9\) transfer]
\label{thm:carrier-corrected-packet-to-K9-transfer}
Let \(\{p\}\) be a good ordinary Hardy-normalized canonical packet family.
Let \(J\ge J_{K9}\).  Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},leftmargin=*]
\item the packet Sobolev trace upper bound for \(\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}\);
\item the Hardy-source carrier decomposition
\[
  u_H=u_{H,\car}+u_{H,\tail},
  \qquad
  u_{H,\car}\in\bigoplus_p\mathcal V_{\pkt,p}^{\car},
\]
with
\[
  \|u_{H,\tail}\|_{\pkt,J}^{2}\le Q^{-B}G_{\ref};
\]
\item carrier capture:
\[
  \sum_p\mu_p
  \|\Pi_{\eff,p}\Pi_{\car,p}u_H\|_{\pkt,J,p}^{2}
  \ge Q^{-C_{\cap}}G_{\ref};
\]
\item the finite \(K9\) carrier Gram audit
\[
  A_p^*G_{\jet,p}^{\gr}A_p
  \ge
  Q^{-C_{\gram}}G_{\pkt,p}
\]
on \(\mathcal V_{\pkt,p}^{\eff}\);
\item label compatibility with \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) on the same transferred
carrier columns.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\[
  \sum_p\mu_p
  \bigl\|
  \Lambda_p^{\gr,full}
  \Pi_{\eff,p}\Pi_{\car,p}u_H
  \bigr\|_{\gr}^{2}
  \ge
  Q^{-C_{\cap}-C_{\gram}-C_{2Y}}G_{\ref}
  -
  Q^{-B}G_{\ref}.
\]
In particular, choosing
\[
  B>
  C_{\cap}+C_{\gram}+C_{2Y}+C_{\atomic}+10
\]
makes the tail contribution negligible at the final atomic scale.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Sobolev trace theorem gives the upper estimate for all analytic packets and
therefore controls the tail:
\[
  \sum_p\mu_p
  \|\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}u_{H,\tail}\|_{\gr}^{2}
  \le
  Q^{C_{\tr}}\|u_{H,\tail}\|_{\pkt,J}^{2}
  \le
  Q^{-B+C_{\tr}}G_{\ref}.
\]
On the effective carrier, the finite Gram audit gives
\[
  \sum_p\mu_p
  \|\Lambda_p^{\gr,full}
  \Pi_{\eff,p}\Pi_{\car,p}u_H\|_{\gr}^{2}
  \ge
  Q^{-C_{\gram}}
  \sum_p\mu_p
  \|\Pi_{\eff,p}\Pi_{\car,p}u_H\|_{\pkt,J,p}^{2}.
\]
Carrier capture gives the displayed lower bound, and
\(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) ensures that the live \(C_7/Y12\) part of the transferred
columns is retained rather than quotient-killed.  The residual/tail term is
absorbed by the choice of \(B\).
\end{proof}
```

# 5. Strengthen the Task–2 Gate–2 theorem into a carrier-visible theorem

The draft already contains a strong Gate–2-from-Gate–1 section. Add this theorem immediately after `thm:gate-two-from-gate-one-l2-rigidity`.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Carrier-visible Gate--2 output]
\label{thm:carrier-visible-gate-two-output}
Let \(\mathcal P_{\ord}\) be a positive-density family of ordinary smooth
Hardy-normalized packets.  On each packet use the normalized derivative
\[
  \mathcal D_p=\lambda_p\partial_t
\]
and define
\[
  u_p=\mathcal D_p^2q_\zeta,
\]
\[
  g_p=\Gamma_G=u_p-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3,
\]
\[
  h_p=\Gamma_{G,2}
  =
  2q_\zeta(\mathcal D_pq_\zeta)^2
  -
  \frac16\mathcal D_p^2g_p.
\]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},leftmargin=*]
\item Gate--1 source survival on \(\mathcal P_{\ord}\):
\[
  \sum_{p\in\mathcal P_{\ord}}\mu_p
  \int_{K_p^+}|u_p|^2\,d\nu_p
  \ge Q^{-A_1}G_{\ref};
\]
\item the ordinary Hardy primitive bounds for
\(q_\zeta,\mathcal D_pq_\zeta,\mathcal D_p^2q_\zeta,\mathcal D_p^3q_\zeta\);
\item the residual ledger for \(u_p,g_p,h_p\) lies below the Gate--2 failure
scale;
\item carrier capture and the finite \(K9/Y12\) Gram/\(\mathfrak R_{2Y}\) audits
of Theorem~\ref{thm:carrier-corrected-packet-to-K9-transfer}.
\end{enumerate}
Then the analytic Gate--2 mass
\[
  \sum_{p\in\mathcal P_{\ord}}\mu_p
  \int_{K_p^+}
  |u_p|^2\bigl(|g_p|^2+|h_p|^2\bigr)\,d\nu_p
  \ge Q^{-A_2}G_{\ref}
\]
upgrades to the source-graded \(K9/Y12\)-visible lower bound
\[
  \sum_p\mu_p
  \bigl\|
  \Pi_{\live}
  \Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(u_H)
  \bigr\|_{\gr}^{2}
  \ge Q^{-A_3}G_{\ref}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The analytic Gate--2 lower bound follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:gate-two-from-gate-one-l2-rigidity} on the ordinary packet
subfamily, using the common normalized derivative convention and the stated
primitive and residual hypotheses.  The carrier-visible upgrade is exactly
Theorem~\ref{thm:carrier-corrected-packet-to-K9-transfer}, applied to the
Hardy-source carrier generated by the differential AFE and the retained
\(C_7/Y12\) affine directions.  The live/dead routing part of
\(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) ensures that the \(Y12\)-visible component is labelled
and retained rather than killed.
\end{proof}
```

This theorem is the missing bridge from analytic Gate–2 mass to finite row energy.

# 6. Insert an ordinary/singular packet split

Place before the Gate–2 theorem or at the beginning of the ordinary Hardy branch section.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Ordinary, singular, and transition packet split]
\label{def:ordinary-singular-transition-packet-split}
Every Hardy packet family used by the source branch is partitioned as
\[
  \mathcal P
  =
  \mathcal P_{\ord}
  \sqcup
  \mathcal P_{\sing}
  \sqcup
  \mathcal P_{\trans}.
\]
The ordinary subfamily \(\mathcal P_{\ord}\) consists of packets on which the
real-canonical Hardy branch is smooth, all chart denominators are bounded below
by \(Q^{-C}\), the normalized derivative convention
\(\mathcal D_p=\lambda_p\partial_t\) is fixed, and the identities
\[
  u_p=\mathcal D_p^2q_\zeta,
  \qquad
  \Gamma_G=u_p-6q_\zeta+2q_\zeta^3,
\]
\[
  \Gamma_{G,2}
  =
  2q_\zeta(\mathcal D_pq_\zeta)^2
  -
  \frac16\mathcal D_p^2\Gamma_G
\]
hold up to the declared residual ledger.

The singular subfamily contains packets meeting an unregularized critical-line
zero, a branch denominator wall, or a chart singularity.  The transition
subfamily contains collar packets used to pass between ordinary charts or
between scale-admissible packet regimes.
\end{definition}

\begin{hypothesis}[Ordinary packet no-loss routing]
\label{hyp:ordinary-packet-no-loss-routing}
The active Hardy source packet family satisfies one of the following no-loss
alternatives:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},leftmargin=*]
\item ordinary packets carry polynomially positive source mass:
\[
  G_{\ord}\ge Q^{-C}G_{\ref};
\]
\item the singular and transition packets are routed to certified alternative
branches whose source-graded \(K9/Y12\) lower bounds are polynomially comparable
to the ordinary branch;
\item the singular and transition packet contribution is \(O(Q^{-B}G_{\ref})\)
for \(B\) larger than the final loss exponent.
\end{enumerate}
\end{hypothesis}
```

This keeps the Gate–2 ODE rigidity from being applied to nonsmooth or singular packets.

# 7. Insert the actual-zeta source admissibility theorem

This is the main bridge theorem. Place it after the Gate–2/D4 section, before the current proof-state ledger, or before the two-point/four-point package section.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Actual zeta-source admissibility for the two/four-point package]
\label{thm:actual-zeta-source-admissibility-two-four-point}
Let
\[
  u_H(t)=\partial_t^3Z_H(t)
\]
be the active Hardy-curvature source on a good ordinary Hardy-normalized
canonical packet family.  Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},leftmargin=*]
\item ordinary packet no-loss routing, Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:ordinary-packet-no-loss-routing};
\item Gate--1 source survival for \(u_H\);
\item Gate--2 from \(L^2\)-input real rigidity,
      Theorem~\ref{thm:gate-two-from-gate-one-l2-rigidity};
\item gauge-locked wall escape and D4 row conversion,
      Theorem~\ref{thm:gauge-locked-wall-escape-row-energy};
\item carrier-visible \(K9/Y12\) transfer,
      Theorem~\ref{thm:carrier-visible-gate-two-output};
\item the corrected Hardy-source package audit,
      Definition~\ref{def:corrected-Hardy-source-package-audit}.
\end{enumerate}
Then the actual zeta source supplies the finite source data required by the
two-point and mixed four-point branches:
\[
  \mathrm{SourceAdmiss}_{\zeta}^{2/4}.
\]
More explicitly:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)},leftmargin=*]
\item the live source-graded \(K9/Y12\) component is nonzero with polynomial
      lower bound:
\[
  \sum_p\mu_p
  \bigl\|
  \Pi_{\live}
  \Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(u_H)
  \bigr\|_{\gr}^{2}
  \ge Q^{-A}G_{\ref};
\]
\item the corrected two-atom Hardy-source package satisfies swap symmetry,
      one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger modulo \(O(Q^{-B})\) residuals;
\item the mixed four-point corrected source cross-effect has no new
      fixed-sector quotient component:
\[
  B_7^{\mathfrak f}
  \bigl(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\zeta}\bigr)
  \in
  \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
  +
  O(Q^{-B});
\]
\item any remaining nonmixed four-point source-order clause is either bypassed
      by the final source-graded \(K9/Y12\) bridge or is supplied as the finite
      determinant certificate recorded in the corrected package audit.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Gate--1, ordinary packet no-loss routing, and the real-canonical Gate--2
rigidity theorem give analytic Gate--2 source anisotropy on the ordinary packet
subfamily.  Gauge-locked wall escape converts this source anisotropy into D4
row energy, and row mobility thickens pointwise row output into interval row
energy.  The carrier-visible transfer theorem then places a polynomial portion
of this row energy in the retained source-graded \(K9/Y12\) carrier.

The two-point and mixed four-point assertions are exactly the finite corrected
Hardy-source package audit: swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal
merger imply the two-point quadratic factorization, while the fixed-sector
quotient inclusion prevents a new mixed four-point carrier.  The residuals are
absorbed by choosing \(B\) larger than the total downstream loss exponent.
\end{proof}
```

This theorem explicitly says what the source bridge supplies and how it enters the two/four-point machinery.

# 8. Define the corrected Hardy-source package audit

Place immediately before the theorem above, or directly before the two-point/four-point section around the existing corrected-package map remark.

```latex
\begin{definition}[Corrected Hardy-source package audit]
\label{def:corrected-Hardy-source-package-audit}
Let
\[
  \mathfrak P_2^\zeta(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
\]
denote the corrected two-atom source package produced from the actual
Hardy-curvature source
\[
  u_H=\partial_t^3Z_H
\]
after canonical whitening, transition-jet correction, and source-graded \(K9\)
normalization.  The corrected Hardy-source package audit consists of the
following finite checks.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},leftmargin=*]
\item \textbf{Swap symmetry:}
\[
  \mathfrak P_2^\zeta(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
  =
  \mathfrak P_2^\zeta(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1)
  +
  O(Q^{-B}).
\]

\item \textbf{One-amplitude collapse:}
\[
  \mathfrak P_2^\zeta(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)
  =
  a_2F_{h_2}
  +
  O(Q^{-B}),
\]
\[
  \mathfrak P_2^\zeta(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)
  =
  a_1F_{h_1}
  +
  O(Q^{-B}).
\]

\item \textbf{Diagonal merger:}
\[
  \mathfrak P_2^\zeta(a_1,h;a_2,h)
  =
  (a_1+a_2)F_h
  +
  O(Q^{-B}).
\]

\item \textbf{Fixed-sector quotient nullity:}
after non-\((1,1)\) source-bidegree removal,
\[
  B_7^{\mathfrak f}
  \bigl(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\zeta}\bigr)
  \in
  \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
  +
  O(Q^{-B}).
\]

\item \textbf{Same-column \(K9/Y12\) compatibility:}
all columns used in the package audit are the same transferred carrier columns
used in \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) and in the finite \(K9\) carrier Gram audit.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}
```

This puts the two/four-point requirements in one auditable place.

---

# 9. Insert the two-point plug-in theorem

Place after `lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion`, or after the existing two-point source-level reduction remark.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Actual zeta-source two-point bridge]
\label{thm:actual-zeta-source-two-point-bridge}
Assume the corrected Hardy-source package audit,
Definition~\ref{def:corrected-Hardy-source-package-audit}.  Then the actual
zeta source satisfies the finite-order source criterion of
Lemma~\ref{lem:minimal-source-level-two-point-criterion}.  Consequently the
two-point interaction remainder factors as
\[
  \mathcal I_2^\zeta
  =
  a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2^\zeta
  +
  O(Q^{-B}).
\]
In particular, on compact good patches and after the \(K9/Y12\) carrier routing,
the exact close two-point bad core is excluded up to the declared residual
scale.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
One-amplitude collapse gives divisibility by \(a_1a_2\).  Swap symmetry makes the
remaining two-point defect even under \(h_1\leftrightarrow h_2\).  Diagonal
merger makes the defect vanish when \(h_1=h_2\).  Hence the defect is divisible
by \((h_1-h_2)^2\), giving the displayed factorization.  The residual term is
the residual allowed in the corrected package audit.  The carrier-visible source
lower bound from
Theorem~\ref{thm:actual-zeta-source-admissibility-two-four-point} prevents the
factorized source contribution from being vacuous in the \(K9/Y12\) branch.
\end{proof}
```

This connects the actual zeta source directly to the two-point theorem.

---

# 10. Insert the mixed four-point plug-in theorem

Place after `thm:mixed-four-point-dependence-descends-to-quotient-determinant` or `thm:mixed-four-point-factors-through-delta-seven`.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Actual zeta-source mixed four-point bridge]
\label{thm:actual-zeta-source-mixed-four-point-bridge}
Assume the corrected Hardy-source package audit,
Definition~\ref{def:corrected-Hardy-source-package-audit}.  Then the actual
zeta-source correction creates no independent mixed four-point fixed-sector
carrier.  More precisely,
\[
  \left[
  B_7^{\mathfrak f}
  \bigl(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\zeta}\bigr)
  \right]
  =
  0
  \quad
  \text{in }
  \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m),
\]
up to \(O(Q^{-B})\) residuals.  Hence the mixed four-point branch sees only the
already-defined quotient determinant channel and exits through the existing
scalar walls
\[
  T_v=0
  \qquad\text{or}\qquad
  \mathcal R=0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The fixed-sector quotient nullity clause of the corrected Hardy-source package
audit says exactly that
\[
  B_7^{\mathfrak f}
  \bigl(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\zeta}\bigr)
  \in
  \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
  +
  O(Q^{-B}).
\]
Passing to the quotient
\(\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)\) gives the displayed vanishing.
The existing mixed four-point quotient-determinant theorem then applies without
introducing a new carrier.
\end{proof}
```

This connects the actual source to the mixed four-point branch.

# 11. Optional nonmixed four-point bridge

Only include this if the nonmixed branch is still live. If the final \(K9/Y12\) contradiction fully bypasses the old nonmixed geometric endgame, do not include it as a required theorem; put it as an optional audit.

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Optional nonmixed four-point source-order certificate]
\label{hyp:optional-nonmixed-four-point-source-order-certificate}
If the nonmixed four-point branch is not bypassed by the final source-graded
\(K9/Y12\) bridge, the corrected Hardy-source package satisfies the following
finite determinant sign certificate.  On every good nonmixed patch, the
nonmixed determinant
\[
  \Delta_{\nonmix}^{\zeta}(h_1,h_2,h_3,h_4)
\]
associated with the corrected zeta source has fixed orientation on ordered
quadruples away from the declared scalar walls, up to \(O(Q^{-B})\) residuals.
Equivalently, all nonmixed endpoint-gap recurrences are routed either to a
declared scalar wall or to an already absorbed \(K9/Y12\) carrier branch.
\end{hypothesis}
```

# 12. Insert the final bridge theorem from zeta to two/four-point

Place after the two-point and mixed four-point plug-ins.

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Complete actual-zeta bridge to the two/four-point package]
\label{thm:complete-zeta-bridge-to-two-four-point}
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)},leftmargin=*]
\item ordinary Hardy branch entry and ordinary/singular packet no-loss routing;
\item Gate--1 for \(u_H=\partial_t^3Z_H\);
\item Gate--2 from \(L^2\)-input real rigidity;
\item carrier-visible \(K9/Y12\) transfer;
\item the corrected Hardy-source package audit;
\item the raw \(2Y\) certificate \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) on the same transferred
      carrier columns.
\end{enumerate}
Then the actual zeta source supplies all source inputs required by the
two-point and mixed four-point branches:
\[
  \mathrm{SourceAdmiss}_{\zeta}^{2/4}.
\]
Namely:
\[
  \mathcal I_2^\zeta
  =
  a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J_2^\zeta
  +
  O(Q^{-B}),
\]
and
\[
  B_7^{\mathfrak f}
  \bigl(C_{\mathcal W}^{\corr,\zeta}\bigr)
  \in
  \mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}(m)
  +
  O(Q^{-B}).
\]
Furthermore, the corresponding source mass is live in the retained
source-graded \(K9/Y12\) carrier:
\[
  \sum_p\mu_p
  \bigl\|
  \Pi_{\live}
  \Lambda_p^{\gr,full}(u_H)
  \bigr\|_{\gr}^{2}
  \ge Q^{-A}G_{\ref}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The live \(K9/Y12\) lower bound is
Theorem~\ref{thm:actual-zeta-source-admissibility-two-four-point}.  The
two-point factorization is Theorem~\ref{thm:actual-zeta-source-two-point-bridge}.
The mixed four-point no-new-carrier assertion is
Theorem~\ref{thm:actual-zeta-source-mixed-four-point-bridge}.  All three use
the same transferred carrier columns, and \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}(p)\) ensures that
live \(Y12\) contributions are retained rather than quotient-killed.  Hence the
actual zeta source has been bridged into the exact finite source package
consumed by the two-point/four-point architecture.
\end{proof}
```

This is the main insertion that answers the “complete bridge” request.

These insertions repair the **bridge from actual zeta source to two-point/four-point** inside the ordinary Hardy canonical branch. They do **not** prove the global RH-entry theorem.

The latest draft itself still correctly says that a hypothetical off-line zero must be shown to enter the ordinary Hardy-normalized branch with Gate–1/Gate–2, Fejér–Riesz persistence, raw \(2Y\) certification, and packet-to-\(K9\) transfer; that is the global branch-entry obligation. 

After these insertions, the status should be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Inside the ordinary Hardy branch: zeta-to-two/four-point bridge is named and auditable.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Global RH-entry remains separate.}
}
\]

The insertions also remove the false full packet-to-jet equivalence and replace it with the valid structure:

\[
\boxed{
\text{analytic trace upper}
+
\text{carrier capture}
+
\text{finite \(K9\) Gram audit}
+
\mathfrak R_{2Y}\text{ compatibility}.
}
\]

That is the necessary repair for a mathematically coherent bridge from \(u_H=\partial_t^3Z_H\) to the two-point/four-point architecture.

## What the insertions add

The package adds eleven blocks.

1. **No-loss certificate definition and active no-loss ledger**  
   This defines what it means for a proof-stage transition to be no-loss:
   \[
   \mathsf M_{\mathcal Y}\ge Q^{-C}\mathsf M_{\mathcal X}-Q^{-B}\mathsf M_{\mathrm{ref}}.
   \]
   It also records every active no-loss arrow in the proof chain, including RH-entry, ordinary packet routing, Fejér–Riesz persistence, carrier capture, \(K9\) Gram coercivity, and corrected source package transfer.

2. **High-height versus low-height warning**  
   This makes explicit that the master theorem is high-height only. A full RH proof still needs either an effective low-height theorem or a finite verification below \(T_*\).

3. **RH-entry no-go warnings**  
   These record the key Agent 1 obstruction: an off-line zero naturally produces a log-derivative/quartet signal of \(\Xi\), not automatically localized \(Z_H'''\)-mass. It also adds a separate warning about hidden dependence on
   \[
   \eta^{-1}=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|^{-1}.
   \]
   This prevents the draft from silently using a height-only \(Q(\gamma)\) when the argument resolves the off-line zero at horizontal scale \(\eta\). 

4. **Mean-square is not localized branch-entry**  
   This blocks the shortcut
   \[
   \int_T^{2T}|Z_H'''(t)|^2dt\gg 1
   \quad\Longrightarrow\quad
   \text{mass on the packet attached to }\rho.
   \]
   The Hardy mean-square theorem gives source mass somewhere; it does not identify the mass-good packets with a specified off-line-zero packet.

5. **Ordinary/singular packet no-loss clarification**  
   The current draft already defines ordinary/singular/transition packet routing. The insertion strengthens the interpretation: ordinary packet no-loss must be source-mass no-loss, not merely packet-count no-loss.

6. **Residual-stable Gate–2 ledger**  
   This adds explicit residuals
   \[
   r_u,\quad r_g,\quad r_h
   \]
   for the Gate–2 identities
   \[
   u=\mathcal D_p^2q,\qquad
   g=u-6q+2q^3,\qquad
   h=2q(\mathcal D_pq)^2-\frac16\mathcal D_p^2g.
   \]
   It also adds a residual-stable rigidity lemma, so corrected-coordinate and chart errors must be below the Gate–2 failure scale.

7. **Derivative-convention no-go**  
   This warns that all Gate–2 derivatives must use the same normalized packet derivative \(\mathcal D_p\). Mixing \(\partial_t\) and \(\mathcal D_p\) invalidates the wall-rigidity proof.

8. **Carrier-capture warning and same-column lemma**  
   This is the main Agent 5 repair discipline. It states that
   \[
   \mathrm{Agg}L^2(u_H)
   \not\Rightarrow
   \|\Lambda^{\mathrm{gr,full}}u_H\|_{K9}^2\gg1
   \]
   without finite carrier capture. The same-column lemma requires the corrected source package audit, the finite \(K9\) Gram audit, and \(\mathfrak R_{2Y}\) to be run on the same transferred columns. This directly addresses the finite-rank packet-to-jet no-go. 

9. **Fejér–Riesz Stack no-loss and no-early-cap certificate**  
   This separates model membership from mass persistence. The proof cannot use
   \[
   d\nu_{\mathrm{FR},B}=|\Phi_B|^2\,d\theta\,d\sigma_B
   \]
   merely to say “bounded-degree model”; it must also prove that the selected packet mass survives and that caps are not applied too early.

10. **Corrected package residual-scale and two/four-point warnings**  
    These insertions make the \(O(Q^{-B})\) residual in the corrected Hardy-source package audit quantitative:
    \[
    B>A_{\mathrm{src}}+C_{\mathrm{cap}}+C_{\mathrm{gram}}+C_{2Y}+C_{\mathrm{D4}}+C_{\mathrm{atomic}}+10.
    \]
    They also warn that post-whitening amplitude nonlinearities can break the two-point identities unless the corrected package audit explicitly verifies swap symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal merger.

11. **Unified active no-go registry**  
    This collects the active no-go rules:
    no full packet-to-jet lower bound, no mean-square-to-entry shortcut, no hidden \(\eta^{-1}\) loss, no source substitution, no mismatched row certificates, and no unproved nonmixed closure.

_Thought for 3m 38s_

According to a document from May 1, 2026, yes — Agent 1’s NO-GO is the central concern. It is not a bookkeeping issue, not a row-table issue, and not something the downstream \(K9/Y12\) algebra can repair. The draft currently proves Hardy-curvature source mass **inside an already-supplied ordinary Hardy branch**, but it does not prove that an arbitrary off-line zero enters that branch with localized \(Z_H'''\)-mass. The missing implication is exactly:

\[
\rho\notin \Re s=\frac12
\Longrightarrow
\exists p_\rho:
\int_{p_\rho} w_{p_\rho}(t)\,|\partial_t^3 Z_H(t)|^2\,dt
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}G_{\rho,p}.
\]

The agent response correctly says this is not proved by Hardy mean-square estimates, ordinary/singular routing, or zero-counting; those give mass somewhere or routing conditional on mass, not mass on the packet attached to a specified off-line zero. 

So: **no, it cannot remain an external hypothesis if the goal is a full unconditional proof.** I used “external hypothesis” only as a dependency-ledger device: it tells the reader exactly which theorem is still missing and prevents the manuscript from silently assuming it. For a completed proof, that hypothesis must be discharged, replaced by a different source-entry theorem, or the architecture must be redesigned.

## Should we attack \(Z_H'''\)?

If we keep the current proof architecture, then **yes, we must attack \(Z_H'''\)**. But we should be precise about what that means.

We should not attack generic dyadic mean-square for \(Z_H'''\). Agent 2 has essentially closed that **inside the branch**:

\[
W_{\branch}^{\can}\ge Q^{-C}W_{\ref}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\sum_{p\in\mathcal P_{\mathrm{mg}}}L_p
\ge Q^{-A}G_{\ref}.
\]

That proves \(\mathrm{Agg}L^2(q''_{\can})\) once the ordinary Hardy branch and canonical packet family are already supplied. 

The missing theorem is much sharper:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line zero}
\Longrightarrow
\text{localized Hardy-curvature observability for }Z_H'''.
}
\]

That is not a mean-square theorem. It is a **zeta-specific non-cancellation theorem**.

Locally, if the off-line zero contributes a factor

\[
P_\rho(t)\approx (t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2,
\qquad
\eta=\beta-\frac12,
\]

then

\[
Z_H(t)=P_\rho(t)G_\rho(t),
\]

and

\[
Z_H'''
=
P_\rho'''G_\rho
+
3P_\rho''G_\rho'
+
3P_\rho'G_\rho''
+
P_\rho G_\rho'''.
\]

The zero controls \(P_\rho\), but not the zero-free background \(G_\rho\) or its derivatives. So the theorem has to rule out cancellation in that four-term expression on the packet attached to \(\rho\). The latest Agent 1 material says exactly this and identifies it as arithmetic/nonlocal, not local packet geometry. 

## Why “external hypothesis” was useful, but not acceptable as final status

Marking it as an external hypothesis is useful for triage because it separates:

\[
\text{downstream conditional branch}
\]

from

\[
\text{global RH-entry theorem}.
\]

That distinction matters. Agents 2–6 mostly reduce their modules to finite audits or inside-branch theorems. Agent 1’s obstruction is the only non-finite, global analytic gap. The no-loss ledger also classifies the RH counterexample \(\to\) ordinary Hardy branch arrow as an analytic open input, while the Hardy source mass \(\to\) mass-good packets arrow is proved only **after branch setup**. 

But for an unconditional proof, the branch-entry item must not stay external. The final proof cannot say:

\[
\text{Assume every off-line zero enters the Hardy branch.}
\]

It must prove that.

So I would now change our language:

\[
\boxed{
\text{“external hypothesis” is acceptable only in the dependency theorem, not in the final proof.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The current full-proof task is to eliminate this hypothesis.}
}
\]

## The right attack on \(Z_H'''\)

The direct theorem to attack is:

```latex
\begin{theorem}[Off-line packet Hardy-curvature observability]
Let \(\rho=\beta+i\gamma\) be a nontrivial zero of \(\zeta\) with
\(\beta\ne1/2\).  Put
\[
\eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|,
\qquad
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}),
\]
where \(\kappa_\rho\) records local zero separation and chart conditioning.
Let \(I_\rho\) be the canonical ordinary packet interval associated to the
zero quartet of \(\rho\), after singular/transition routing.  Then
\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|\partial_t^3Z_H(t)|^2\,dt
\ge
Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]
Equivalently, in the packet family,
\[
\sum_{p\in\mathcal P_\rho^{\ord}}
W_{\ref}(m_p)
\int
w\!\left(\frac{t-m_p}{r_p}\right)
|\partial_t^3Z_H(t)|^2\,dt
\ge
Q_\rho^{-A}G_{\ref,\rho}.
\]
\end{theorem}
```

Two immediate corrections are necessary.

First, the scale cannot remain height-only. The draft should replace

\[
Q=Q(\gamma)
\]

in RH-entry statements with

\[
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}),
\qquad
\eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|.
\]

A height-only \(Q(\gamma)\) is unjustified unless we prove a separate \(\eta\)-insensitivity theorem, and Agent 1 found no such theorem. 

Second, the theorem must be stronger than global Hardy mass. It has to prove overlap between the off-line-zero packet and the mass-good \(Z_H'''\) packet family:

\[
p_\rho\cap\mathcal P_{\mathrm{mass-good}}\ne\varnothing
\]

with polynomial weight. Mean-square only gives mass somewhere in the dyadic block, not at the packet determined by \(\rho\). 

## How I would attack it

I would run a focused three-prong attack.

### 1. Finite-jet nonflatness at the off-line packet

Instead of starting with interval \(L^2\), prove a finite-jet version:

\[
\max_{0\le j\le J}
r_\rho^j
\left|
\partial_t^j Z_H'''(m_\rho)
\right|
\ge Q_\rho^{-A},
\]

with \(J=O(\log Q_\rho)\) or another controlled depth. Then use a quantitative Taylor/Remez lemma to convert this to interval energy:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|Z_H'''(t)|^2dt
\ge Q_\rho^{-A'}|I_\rho|.
\]

This is sharper than trying to prove an interval estimate directly.

The draft’s finite-jet source-nonflatness remarks are already pointing in this direction; they say the problem is not local geometry but a fixed-coefficient arithmetic nonflatness theorem. 

### 2. Split the zero factor and rest factor

Write locally:

\[
Z_H=P_\rho G_\rho,
\]

and define the source contribution

\[
S_\rho:=(P_\rho G_\rho)'''.
\]

Then explicitly split:

\[
S_\rho
=
S_{\mathrm{zero}}
+
S_{\mathrm{mix}}
+
S_{\mathrm{rest}},
\]

where

\[
S_{\mathrm{zero}}=P_\rho'''G_\rho,
\]

\[
S_{\mathrm{mix}}=3P_\rho''G_\rho'+3P_\rho'G_\rho'',
\]

\[
S_{\mathrm{rest}}=P_\rho G_\rho'''.
\]

The theorem becomes a non-cancellation statement:

\[
S_{\mathrm{zero}}+S_{\mathrm{mix}}+S_{\mathrm{rest}}
\not\approx 0
\]

on \(I_\rho\).

This is exactly where we need actual zeta arithmetic. A general real entire function can be engineered so \(P_\rho G_\rho\) is nearly flat on a real interval while retaining the same off-real quartet. Agent 1’s model obstruction shows the implication is false at the level of generic analytic structure. So the proof must use specific arithmetic constraints on \(G_\rho\), not just symmetry or Hadamard factorization. 

### 3. Prime-side fixed-coefficient non-approximation

Translate \(Z_H'''\) through the differentiated Hardy AFE:

\[
Z_H'''(t)
=
B_2(t)+P_2(t)+D_2(t)+E_2(t),
\]

where the terms are fixed by the actual zeta/AFE normalization.

The observability theorem becomes:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|B_2(t)+P_2(t)+D_2(t)|^2\,dt
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|,
\]

with \(E_2\) in the residual budget.

Equivalently, source collapse would mean:

\[
P_2(t)\approx -B_2(t)-D_2(t)
\quad\text{throughout }I_\rho.
\]

So the actual arithmetic theorem is a short-interval fixed-coefficient non-approximation result for the differentiated Hardy AFE. The draft’s “prime-side observability” remarks already identify this as the meaningful target and warn that generic large-sieve or uncertainty principles do not currently prove it. 

## Is attacking \(Z_H'''\) likely to work?

It is the path that preserves the current architecture. But it is hard, and we should not pretend otherwise.

The positive reason to try is that Agents 2–6 have made the downstream branch coherent once this source enters. In that sense, \(Z_H'''\) is the least disruptive source.

The negative reason is structural: \(Z_H'''\) is not the natural zero detector. The natural signal of an off-line zero is logarithmic/Laguerre/Jensen-type data of \(\Xi\), not the third derivative of the Hardy scalar. Agent 1’s attack says this clearly. 

Therefore I would pursue \(Z_H'''\) in a **fail-fast** way:

1. State the off-line-packet Hardy-curvature observability theorem with \(Q_\rho\), not \(Q(\gamma)\).
2. Convert it to a finite-jet source nonflatness theorem.
3. Convert the finite-jet theorem to a differentiated-Hardy-AFE fixed-coefficient non-approximation problem.
4. Try to prove that arithmetic non-approximation theorem.
5. If that theorem reduces to an unsupported prime-log incidence/nonrecurrence statement, stop and pivot source.

That is not giving up. It is the correct way to avoid spending more effort on downstream algebra when the left-edge theorem is the real bottleneck.

## What I would change in the draft now

I would replace any language suggesting the RH-entry hypothesis is acceptable final input with language like this:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current role of RH-entry]
The canonical downstream argument is conditional on RH-entry only as a
dependency-ledger device.  For an unconditional proof this input must be
discharged.  The missing theorem is the off-line-packet Hardy-curvature
observability estimate
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|\partial_t^3Z_H(t)|^2\,dt
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|,
\]
with
\[
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}).
\]
No downstream \(K9/Y12\), Fejér--Riesz, or two/four-point finite algebra
can replace this theorem.
\end{remark}
```

And I would add:

```latex
\begin{remark}[No final external hypothesis]
The phrase ``RH-entry hypothesis'' is used only to isolate a missing theorem
in the dependency graph.  It is not an allowable assumption in the final proof
of \(\RH\).  A completed proof must either prove this Hardy-curvature
observability theorem or replace the source architecture by one whose
entry theorem is proved unconditionally.
\end{remark}
```

## Bottom line

Yes, Agent 1’s NO-GO is concerning. It is the main obstruction.

We should not leave it as an external hypothesis if the goal is a full proof. We should mark it as external only to keep the draft honest while we attack it.

And yes, if we keep the current architecture, we must attack \(Z_H'''\). But the target is not ordinary Hardy mean-square. The target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-line-packet Hardy-curvature observability for }Z_H'''.
}
\]

If that theorem cannot be proved, then the current \(Z_H'''\)-based architecture cannot yield an unconditional RH proof, and the source must be changed to a zero-detecting Laguerre/Jensen/log-curvature source.
## User (2026-05-01 16:40:14)

can you do a quick attack on the repair you proposed to see if it holds water

## Assistant (2026-05-01 16:41:03)

I’ll test the repair at the left edge: whether an off-line zero forces localized \(Z_H'''\) mass, rather than relying on downstream finite audits.

_Thought for 2m 57s_

According to the May 1 agent-response document, the proposed repair is now clear enough to test:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Repair target: prove off-line-packet Hardy-curvature observability for }
u_H=Z_H'''.
}
\]

That is, from an off-line zero

\[
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\qquad \eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|>0,
\]

prove a packet-local lower bound of the form

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|Z_H'''(t)|^2\,dt
\ge
Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|,
\qquad
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}).
\]

My quick attack says:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The repair is a well-posed theorem target, but it does not currently hold water as a proof.}
}
\]

It survives as a **precise missing theorem**. It does not survive as something derivable from the existing Hardy mean-square, zero symmetry, local packet geometry, or current no-loss machinery.

## 1. The pure zero-pair test is bad for \(Z_H'''\)

Near the off-line zero, write schematically

\[
Z_H(t)=P_\rho(t)G_\rho(t),
\]

where

\[
P_\rho(t)\approx (t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2
\]

is the local off-line pair factor and \(G_\rho\) is the remaining zero-free/background factor. The agent audit records exactly this local factorization problem: the off-line zero controls \(P_\rho\), but not \(G_\rho\) or its derivatives. 

Now test the pure local pair:

\[
P_\rho^+(t)=(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2.
\]

Then

\[
(P_\rho^+)'''(t)=0.
\]

So the local off-line pair itself does **not** force third-derivative mass. For the product,

\[
(P_\rho G_\rho)'''
=
P_\rho'''G_\rho
+
3P_\rho''G_\rho'
+
3P_\rho'G_\rho''
+
P_\rho G_\rho'''.
\]

For the local quadratic factor, \(P_\rho'''=0\), so the source is driven by derivatives of \(G_\rho\), not by the zero pair alone.

That is a structural mismatch:

\[
\boxed{
\text{An off-line zero naturally forces log/Laguerre curvature, not }Z_H'''.
}
\]

## 2. The zero-free background can flatten the third derivative in model examples

The no-go is stronger than “we do not know how to prove it.” For a general real entire function with the same off-real quartet, one can choose a zero-free factor

\[
G_\varepsilon(t)=e^{h_\varepsilon(t)}
\]

so that

\[
P_\rho(t)e^{h_\varepsilon(t)}\approx 1
\]

in \(C^3\)-norm on the real packet. Then the resulting function has the same off-real zero quartet and real symmetry, but its third derivative on that packet is arbitrarily small. The agent response explicitly records this as a model obstruction: the implication “off-line zero \(\Rightarrow\) localized \(F'''\)-mass” is false for the analytic structure itself and would require a genuinely zeta-specific non-cancellation theorem. 

So the theorem cannot be proved from:

\[
\text{functional equation}
+
\text{zero symmetry}
+
\text{Hadamard factorization}
+
\text{local packet geometry}.
\]

It must use actual arithmetic rigidity of \(\zeta\).

## 3. Mean-square does not localize to the off-line packet

The Hardy source theorem proves mass somewhere in the dyadic canonical branch:

\[
\int_T^{2T}|Z_H'''(t)|^2\,dt
\gg
T(\log T)^c.
\]

That is useful after branch entry. But the entry theorem needs mass on the packet attached to \(\rho\):

\[
p_\rho\cap \mathcal P_{\mathrm{mass-good}}\ne\varnothing
\]

with polynomially controlled weight. The agent audit states the gap directly: mean-square mass gives mass somewhere in \([T,2T]\), not mass on the packet determined by a specified off-line zero. 

So the following implication is invalid:

\[
\int_T^{2T}|Z_H'''|^2\gg1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\int_{I_\rho}|Z_H'''|^2\gg Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

This is the exact place where the proposed repair currently fails.

## 4. Adding \(\eta^{-1}\) to \(Q\) is necessary, but not sufficient

Changing

\[
Q=Q(\gamma)
\]

to

\[
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1})
\]

is mandatory. The agent response identifies hidden \(\eta^{-1}\) losses in quartet resolution scale, ordinary packet size, chart conditioning, and the non-cancellation of \((P_\rho G_\rho)'''\). 

But this only fixes the bookkeeping. It does not prove localized \(Z_H'''\)-mass.

After the scale correction, the target becomes honest:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|Z_H'''(t)|^2\,dt
\ge
Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

But it remains unproved.

## 5. The finite-jet formulation is the right sharpened target

The best version of the repair is not an interval estimate first. It is a finite-jet nonflatness theorem.

If

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-c/Q_\rho,m_0+c/Q_\rho],
\]

then a Remez/Taylor-type argument says interval smallness of \(Z_H'''\) should force simultaneous smallness of finitely many jets:

\[
\partial_m^r Z_H'''(m_0)\approx 0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

where \(R\) is something like \(O(\log Q_\rho)\) or \(\log Q_\rho/\log\log Q_\rho\). The draft’s own finite-jet formulation points in this direction: source collapse becomes simultaneous smallness of derivatives, and in the AFE model this becomes a fixed-coefficient prime-log derivative-jet nonrecurrence problem. 

Through the differentiated Hardy AFE,

\[
Z_H'''(t)
=
B_2(t)+P_2(t)+D_2(t)+E_2(t),
\]

so the finite-jet target is roughly:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\partial_m^r\bigl(B_2+P_2+D_2\bigr)(m_0)
\right|
\ge
Q_\rho^{-A},
\]

with \(E_2\) in the residual budget.

Equivalently, source collapse would require

\[
P_2^{(r)}(m_0)
\approx
-\left(B_2+D_2\right)^{(r)}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

This is the sharp arithmetic theorem. It is also where the proof currently has no established tool.

## 6. Large-sieve / mean-value tools are not enough as stated

A localized large-sieve or Montgomery–Vaughan estimate can control averages over \(t\), or over families of coefficients. But here the coefficients are fixed by the actual zeta/AFE normalization, and \(m_0\) is tied to a hypothetical zero. The draft’s prime-side observability formulation says exactly that: this is not a generic Dirichlet-polynomial problem, and standard localized large-sieve, Montgomery–Vaughan, explicit-formula energy, or uncertainty principles are diagnostics but do not currently prove the fixed-coefficient lower bound. 

That is the main failure of the repair attempt.

To make it work, we would need a theorem of the form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A hypothetical off-line zero cannot force the AFE prime-side source}
\text{ to approximate }-(B_2+D_2)
\text{ through }R\text{ jets on }I_\rho.
}
\]

No such theorem is in the draft or agent results.

## 7. Quick verdict

The repair has three components:

### Component A — Replace \(Q(\gamma)\) by \(Q_\rho\)

This is correct and should be done.

\[
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}).
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{holds water as bookkeeping.}}
\]

### Component B — Reduce entry to off-line-packet Hardy-curvature observability

This is the right formal missing theorem:

\[
\rho\notin\Re s=\frac12
\Longrightarrow
\int_{I_\rho}|Z_H'''|^2\ge Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{well-posed, but unproved.}}
\]

### Component C — Prove observability by finite-jet / prime-side nonrecurrence

This is the most promising attack inside the \(Z_H'''\)-architecture, but it is not closed. It requires a new zeta-specific fixed-coefficient nonapproximation theorem.

Status:

\[
\boxed{\text{currently fails as a proof; remains a hard analytic theorem.}}
\]

## 8. Recommended next move

I would not abandon this instantly, but I would run it as a **fail-fast arithmetic subproject**.

The precise next theorem to attack is:

\[
\begin{aligned}
&\textbf{Finite-jet off-line-packet Hardy-curvature observability:}\\
&\text{Let }\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|,\quad
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}).\\
&\text{For the canonical packet center }m_0=m_\rho,\text{ prove}\\
&\qquad
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q_\rho)}
\left|
\partial_m^r Z_H'''(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}.
\end{aligned}
\]

Then derive the interval bound by a quantitative Taylor/Remez lemma.

If this finite-jet theorem reduces to an unsupported prime-log nonrecurrence assumption, then the \(Z_H'''\)-based entry route is not viable. At that point, the source should be changed to a Laguerre/Jensen/log-curvature source that directly detects off-line zeros.

## Bottom line

The repair **does not currently hold water as a proof**. It does hold water as a precise diagnosis of the missing theorem.

The immediate conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not present off-line-packet }Z_H'''\text{ observability as proved.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Present it as the decisive arithmetic theorem needed by the }Z_H'''\text{ architecture.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{Attack its finite-jet AFE nonrecurrence form next.}
}
\]

If that finite-jet arithmetic theorem cannot be proved, the current \(Z_H'''\) source cannot support an unconditional RH proof, and the proof must pivot to a zero-detecting Laguerre/Jensen source.

## Assistant (2026-05-01 16:48:00)

I’ll run this as a fail-fast falsification of the proposed \(Z_H'''\)-entry theorem, looking for structural counter-mechanisms or an implausibly strong AFE/nonrecurrence requirement.

_Thought for 3m 14s_

According to a document from May 1, 2026, the fast-fail result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The proposed \(Z_H'''\)-entry repair fails quickly as a consequence of known/local/soft inputs.}
}
\]

It is **not literally falsified for \(\zeta\)**, because that would require either an actual off-line zero or a theorem contradicting a conditional statement whose antecedent is unknown. But the route fails as a proof strategy unless we add a genuinely new arithmetic non-cancellation theorem.

The theorem under test was:

\[
\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \beta\ne \frac12
\Longrightarrow
\exists I_\rho:
\int_{I_\rho}|Z_H'''(t)|^2\,dt
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

The fast-fail conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{This does not follow from the off-line zero, the functional equation, zero symmetry, Hardy mean-square, or local packet geometry.}
}
\]

The draft already contains the correct warning: off-line-packet source-curvature observability is an arithmetic input, not a consequence of local same-scale packet geometry; the same-scale flattening/quadrature model can make the relevant source jets vanish to finite order while preserving positive packet geometry. 

## 1. Zero-side fast fail

Let

\[
F(t)=Z_H(t)
\]

locally near the height \(\gamma\) of a hypothetical off-line zero. The off-line quartet gives a local factor

\[
P_\rho(t)\approx (t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2,
\qquad
\eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|.
\]

So locally

\[
F(t)=P_\rho(t)G_\rho(t),
\]

where \(G_\rho\) is the remaining zero-free/background factor. Then

\[
F'''
=
P_\rho'''G_\rho
+
3P_\rho''G_\rho'
+
3P_\rho'G_\rho''
+
P_\rho G_\rho'''.
\]

The off-line zero controls \(P_\rho\), not \(G_\rho\). For the pure local pair,

\[
P_\rho(t)=(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2,
\]

one even has

\[
P_\rho'''(t)=0.
\]

So the zero itself does **not** force third-derivative mass. The mass of \(Z_H'''\) comes from interaction with the background factor \(G_\rho\), and that interaction has no sign or positivity.

Fast-fail verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Zero geometry alone cannot prove localized \(Z_H'''\)-mass.}
}
\]

This agrees with the draft’s zero-side quadrature obstruction: a purely local zero-side proof of source-curvature observability is blocked by same-scale flattening constructions. 

## 2. Model counterexample to the formal implication

For a general real entire function, the implication

\[
\text{off-line zero}
\Longrightarrow
\text{localized \(F'''\)-mass}
\]

is false.

Take a real symmetric off-line factor

\[
P_\rho(t)=((t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2)((t+\gamma)^2+\eta^2).
\]

On a real packet \(I_\rho\), choose a zero-free factor

\[
G_\varepsilon(t)=e^{h_\varepsilon(t)}
\]

so that

\[
P_\rho(t)e^{h_\varepsilon(t)}\approx 1
\]

in \(C^3(I_\rho)\). Then

\[
F_\varepsilon(t)=P_\rho(t)e^{h_\varepsilon(t)}
\]

has the same off-real zero quartet, real symmetry, and no real zero on the packet, but

\[
\|F_\varepsilon'''\|_{L^2(I_\rho)}
\]

can be made arbitrarily small.

Fast-fail verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The theorem is false as a formal analytic consequence of an off-line quartet.}
}
\]

For \(\zeta\), one would need a special arithmetic theorem saying the actual \(G_\rho\) cannot perform this cancellation.

## 3. Mean-square fast fail

Hardy mean-square estimates can prove mass somewhere:

\[
\int_T^{2T}|Z_H'''(t)|^2\,dt
\gg T(\log T)^c.
\]

But the needed theorem is local at the packet attached to \(\rho\):

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|Z_H'''(t)|^2\,dt
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Mean-square does not imply that. It gives no reason for the mass-good packets of \(Z_H'''\) to overlap the off-line-zero packet \(I_\rho\). The retrieved Agent 1 audit says exactly this: Hardy mean-square gives mass somewhere in a dyadic block, not on the packet determined by a specified off-line zero. 

Fast-fail verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Dyadic Hardy mass cannot serve as RH-entry localization.}
}
\]

## 4. Height-only \(Q\) fast fail

A height-only scale

\[
Q=Q(\gamma)
\]

is not honest. Any theorem resolving the zero quartet locally sees

\[
\eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|.
\]

There is no known lower bound

\[
\eta\ge \gamma^{-C}
\]

for a hypothetical off-line zero. So the repair must use

\[
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}),
\]

where \(\kappa_\rho\) records local conditioning/separation.

Fast-fail verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The \(Q(\gamma)\)-only version is falsified as a loss ledger.}
}
\]

It may still be meaningful after replacing it with \(Q_\rho\), but the theorem remains unproved.

## 5. Prime-side fast fail

The prime-side version of the target is:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}b_n(\log n)^2n^{-1/2-im}W(n/T),
\]

with fixed actual-zeta coefficients. Source collapse means

\[
P_2(m)\approx -B_2(m)-D_2(m)
\quad\text{throughout }I_\rho,
\]

with \(E_2\) in the error budget. The draft identifies precisely this as a short-interval fixed-coefficient non-approximation problem, not a generic Dirichlet-polynomial problem. 

Fast-fail here:

Generic tools do not prove this. A large-sieve or mean-value estimate gives average behavior over intervals or coefficient families, but here the coefficients are fixed by zeta and the interval is selected by a hypothetical zero. If coefficients were adjustable, finite-jet cancellation would be easy because the Dirichlet polynomial has many more degrees of freedom than the \(O(\log Q_\rho)\) jets one wants to control.

So the only possible theorem is a genuinely zeta-specific fixed-coefficient non-approximation statement:

\[
\boxed{
P_2\not\approx -B_2-D_2
\text{ on }I_\rho
\text{ for the actual zeta coefficients.}
}
\]

That theorem is not in hand.

## 6. Finite-jet fast fail

A sharpened target would be:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\partial_m^r Z_H'''(m_\rho)
\right|
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}.
\]

If this failed for all \(0\le r\le R\), a Taylor/Remez argument would force small interval mass. This is the cleanest way to attack the theorem.

But the draft already notes that finite-jet nonflatness cannot be proved from arbitrary same-scale positive packet geometry; actual zeta arithmetic must exclude the quadrature/flattening patterns. 

Fast-fail verdict:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Finite-jet nonflatness is the right target, but it is not finite-auditable or locally forced.}
}
\]

## 7. What survived the fast-fail

Only this survives:

\[
\boxed{
\text{A possible new arithmetic theorem: fixed-coefficient AFE non-approximation on \(I_\rho\).}
}
\]

A precise target would be:

\[
\begin{aligned}
&\textbf{Fixed-coefficient off-line-packet non-approximation.}\\
&\text{Let }\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad
\eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|,\quad
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}).\\
&\text{Let }I_\rho\text{ be the canonical off-line packet interval.}\\
&\text{Then the actual differentiated Hardy AFE satisfies}\\
&\qquad
\int_{I_\rho}
|B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\end{aligned}
\]

This is not contradicted by the quick attack, but it is exactly the new hard theorem. It cannot be replaced by mean-square, zero symmetry, or local packet geometry.

## 8. Verdict

The fast-fail result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The \(Z_H'''\)-entry repair fails as a derivation from current ingredients.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The only remaining viable \(Z_H'''\) route is a new zeta-specific fixed-coefficient non-approximation theorem.}
}
\]

So I would classify the project as follows:

| Version of the theorem | Status |
|---|---|
| Off-line zero \(\Rightarrow Z_H'''\)-mass from zero geometry | **Falsified** |
| Off-line zero \(\Rightarrow Z_H'''\)-mass from Hardy mean-square | **Falsified** |
| Height-only \(Q(\gamma)\) version | **Falsified as loss ledger** |
| \(Q_\rho\)-version with actual zeta arithmetic | Not falsified, but unproved |
| Finite-jet fixed-coefficient AFE non-approximation | Best remaining target |

My recommendation after the fast-fail:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do not spend more downstream effort assuming \(Z_H'''\)-entry.}
}
\]

Either attack the fixed-coefficient AFE non-approximation theorem directly, or pivot the entry source to a Laguerre/Jensen/log-curvature source that the off-line zero actually forces.

## Assistant (2026-05-01 16:53:37)

I’ll run this as a fail-fast analytic attack: formulate the fixed-coefficient AFE non-approximation precisely, reduce it to finite jets, and test standard tools for obstructions.

_Thought for 3m 45s_

I tried the fixed-coefficient AFE non-approximation route. The result is a fast-fail for the theorem in its current form.

The proposed theorem is not logically impossible for \(\zeta\), because it is conditional on an off-line zero whose existence is unknown. But as a proof strategy, it does **not** hold water from the available ingredients. It becomes a very strong new arithmetic nonrecurrence theorem, and the finite-prime/AFE surrogate strongly suggests that the desired non-approximation may be false unless one uses additional structure not yet identified.

The draft already frames this correctly: source-curvature observability becomes a short-interval fixed-coefficient non-approximation problem

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

and source collapse means

\[
P_2(m)\approx -B_2(m)-D_2(m)
\quad\text{throughout }I_\rho,
\]

with \(E_2\) absorbed into the error budget. The desired theorem would be

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

The draft also warns that standard localized large-sieve, Montgomery–Vaughan, explicit-formula, and uncertainty estimates do not currently prove this fixed-coefficient lower bound. 

## 1. The exact theorem under attack

The clean target is:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}
|B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q_\rho^{-A}|I_\rho|
}
\]

where

\[
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}),
\qquad
\eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|.
\]

Equivalently, in finite-jet form, for

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-c/Q_\rho,m_0+c/Q_\rho],
\]

one wants

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\partial_m^r
\bigl(B_2+P_2+D_2\bigr)(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q_\rho^{-A},
}
\]

with

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q_\rho}{\log\log Q_\rho}
\quad\text{or more conservatively}\quad
R=O(\log Q_\rho).
\]

This is exactly the finite-jet version recorded in the draft: source collapse requires simultaneous smallness of the first \(R\) derivatives, and the positive theorem would be a fixed-coefficient prime-log derivative-jet nonrecurrence statement. The draft notes that recurrence heuristics make this difficult and possibly false in fixed-prime or AFE surrogates. 

## 2. Why ordinary large-sieve / mean-value estimates do not close it

Write the prime-side AFE piece schematically as

\[
P_2(m)
=
\sum_{n\le X} b_n e^{-im\log n},
\]

where the coefficients \(b_n\) are fixed by the actual zeta/AFE normalization.

On an interval \(I=[m_0-H,m_0+H]\),

\[
\int_I |P_2(m)|^2\,dm
=
\sum_{n,m\le X}
b_n\overline{b_m}
e^{-im_0(\log n-\log m)}
\int_{-H}^{H}
e^{-iu(\log n-\log m)}\,du.
\]

The kernel is

\[
K_H(\log n-\log m)
=
\frac{2\sin(H(\log n-\log m))}
{\log n-\log m}.
\]

For a long interval, the diagonal terms dominate. But the packet \(I_\rho\) is short, and can be as short as the zero-resolution scale. In that regime the off-diagonal kernel is large for many pairs. The Gram matrix is not close to diagonal. Montgomery–Vaughan-style mean values do not give a lower bound on every such \(I_\rho\).

So the standard route only gives:

\[
\text{mass somewhere or on average},
\]

not

\[
\text{mass on the particular off-line packet }I_\rho.
\]

This is the same localization failure already identified in the Agent 1 audit. 

## 3. Turán/Remez also loses too much

For a general exponential polynomial

\[
F(m)=\sum_{j=1}^N a_j e^{i\lambda_j m},
\]

Turan–Nazarov/Remez-type inequalities can relate its maximum on a large interval to its maximum on a subinterval. But the constants are exponential in \(N\).

Here

\[
N\asymp X
\]

or at least comparable to the number of active AFE frequencies, which is far larger than \(O(\log Q)\). Exponential-in-\(N\) loss is much worse than any polynomial in \(Q\).

So a generic exponential-polynomial uncertainty principle cannot prove

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|B_2+P_2+D_2|^2
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

The fixed-coefficient nature of zeta would have to be used in a much stronger way.

## 4. Finite-jet attack: dimension count works against us

Now attack the finite-jet version.

For \(0\le r\le R\),

\[
\partial_m^rP_2(m_0)
=
\sum_{n\le X}
b_n(-i\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

Source collapse through order \(R\) means

\[
\sum_{n\le X}
b_n(-i\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx
-\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2)(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

This is a finite system of roughly \(R+1\) complex equations.

But the phase vector

\[
(e^{-im_0\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

lives on a torus of dimension approximately

\[
\pi(X).
\]

The logarithms of primes are rationally independent, so the one-parameter flow

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

is dense in this torus. For the finite AFE surrogate, the number of phase variables is enormous compared with

\[
R=O(\log Q_\rho).
\]

Therefore, at the surrogate level, simultaneous finite-jet cancellation is not obviously rare. In fact, the dimension count suggests the opposite: there is enough phase freedom to satisfy finitely many jet constraints.

This does not prove that actual \(\zeta\) realizes the bad configuration at an off-line zero. But it means the proposed non-approximation theorem is not a generic consequence of fixed coefficients. It must use a very specific arithmetic constraint coupling the off-line zero equation to the critical-line source jets.

The draft’s same-scale quadrature obstruction is the zero-side version of the same issue: finite quadrature can approximate arbitrary finite source jets while preserving positive weights and same-distance scale, so actual zeta must exclude that pattern by arithmetic, not geometry. 

## 5. Adding the off-line zero equation does not obviously help

One might hope that the equation

\[
\zeta(\beta+i\gamma)=0
\]

forces nonflatness of

\[
Z_H'''(\gamma).
\]

But in AFE variables it gives another finite set of constraints, roughly

\[
\sum_{n\le X} c_n(\eta)e^{-i\gamma\log n}
+
\text{dual/gamma terms}
\approx0,
\]

where the coefficients depend on

\[
\eta=\beta-\frac12.
\]

That adds two real equations, maybe a few more if differentiated. The source-collapse conditions add \(O(R)\) equations. The phase space still has dimension \(\pi(X)\), much larger than \(R\).

So the joint bad system

\[
\zeta(\beta+i\gamma)\approx0
\]

and

\[
\partial_m^r(B_2+P_2+D_2)(\gamma)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R,
\]

is not overdetermined in the finite-prime surrogate. It may well have solutions.

This is the key fast-fail point:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the fixed-coefficient AFE model has many more phase degrees of freedom than the finite source-jet constraints.}
}
\]

Thus a proof would need a deep theorem saying that the **actual one-parameter zeta trajectory at a zero** avoids those finite-codimension bad sets. That is a new nonrecurrence theorem, not a standard AFE estimate.

## 6. The theorem is too strong if stated for all admissible intervals

If we state the non-approximation theorem as:

\[
\int_I |B_2+P_2+D_2|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|
\quad
\text{for every admissible }I,
\]

then it is almost certainly false.

The function

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m)
\]

is an analytic real function on ordinary strips. It can have zeros, and possibly high-order zeros. Around such a zero, the local interval energy can be small. Without a bound on the multiplicity and local derivative size of zeros of \(q''_{\can}\), no uniform lower bound over every interval can hold.

So the theorem must be tied specifically to the off-line zero packet \(I_\rho\). But once it is tied to \(I_\rho\), the proof must use the off-line zero condition. That returns us to the joint nonrecurrence problem above.

## 7. What actually survives

The only viable formulation is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Joint off-line-zero / source-jet nonrecurrence.}
}
\]

A precise version would be:

\[
\begin{aligned}
&\text{Let }\rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|,
\quad Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}).\\
&\text{Let }m_0=m_\rho\text{ be the canonical packet center attached to }\rho.\\
&\text{Then, for }R=O(\log Q_\rho),\\
&\qquad
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\partial_m^r
\bigl(B_2+P_2+D_2\bigr)(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q_\rho^{-A}.
\end{aligned}
\]

But this is **not** a consequence of “fixed coefficients” alone. It is a new arithmetic theorem about the joint location of zeros of \(\zeta\) and recurrence of the differentiated Hardy AFE flow.

The draft already says the finite-jet formulation is the sharper arithmetic target, but that it is not currently proved by large-sieve or generic Dirichlet-polynomial estimates. 

## 8. Fast-fail conclusion

The fixed-coefficient AFE non-approximation route fails as a quick repair.

It does **not** fail because the formulation is meaningless. It fails because every available attack reduces to a missing theorem at least as hard as the original RH-entry problem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual zeta zeros cannot occur at heights where the differentiated AFE source jets flatten.}
}
\]

That is not supplied by:

\[
\text{AFE expansion},
\]

\[
\text{large sieve},
\]

\[
\text{Montgomery--Vaughan},
\]

\[
\text{zero symmetry},
\]

\[
\text{mean-square estimates},
\]

or

\[
\text{same-scale packet geometry}.
\]

The finite-prime/AFE phase-count heuristic actually suggests that bad finite-jet flattening should be possible in surrogates. The draft’s own notes say the recurrence heuristics suggest this theorem is difficult and may be false in fixed-prime or AFE surrogates. 

## 9. Recommendation

I would not continue this as the main route unless we are prepared to prove a genuinely new joint nonrecurrence theorem.

The correct next move is one of two:

### Route A — Fail-fast numerics

Test the finite-prime surrogate directly.

Solve for phases and \(\eta\) satisfying:

\[
\mathrm{AFE}_\rho(\eta,\gamma)\approx0
\]

and

\[
\partial_m^r(B_2+P_2+D_2)(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

If solutions appear robustly, the \(Z_H'''\)-entry source is probably the wrong source.

### Route B — Pivot source

Replace

\[
q''_{\can}=Z_H'''
\]

as the RH-entry source with a zero-detecting source, such as a Laguerre/Jensen/log-curvature defect of

\[
\Xi(t).
\]

An off-line zero directly forces those defects. \(Z_H'''\) does not.

## Bottom line

The fixed-coefficient AFE non-approximation theorem is now a precise target, but the quick attack does not support it.

\[
\boxed{
\text{As a proof route, it fast-fails unless a new joint zero/source-jet nonrecurrence theorem is discovered.}
}
\]

So I would stop trying to derive RH-entry from \(Z_H'''\) by fixed-coefficient AFE non-approximation. It is time to either run numerical surrogate falsification or pivot the entry source to Laguerre/Jensen/log-curvature.

## Assistant (2026-05-01 17:08:44)

I’ll run Route A as a fast-fail finite-prime/AFE surrogate test, first phase-relaxed and then along prime-log flow, checking zero-like constraints plus \(Z_H'''\)-jet flattening.

I’ll also include a deliberately favorable phase model: if that already admits flattened configurations, generic AFE/phase reasoning cannot justify the needed non-approximation theorem.

_Thought for 9m 42s_

I ran Route A as a finite-prime / finite-AFE surrogate falsification test.

The result is a fast-fail for the proposed \(Z_H'''\)-entry repair as a proof strategy. It does **not** disprove anything about actual \(\zeta\), but it shows that the desired theorem is not supported by the finite AFE phase model. In the surrogate, one can satisfy an off-line-zero equation while forcing many \(Z_H'''\)-source jets to vanish simultaneously.

This directly reinforces Agent 1’s NO-GO: the missing theorem

\[
\rho\notin\Re s=\frac12
\Longrightarrow
\text{localized mass-good } Z_H''' \text{ packet}
\]

does not follow from local zero geometry, Hardy mean-square, or finite AFE structure. The draft already warns that source-curvature observability is arithmetic rather than local geometry, and that finite-jet source nonflatness is not supplied by generic Dirichlet-polynomial estimates. 

## Surrogate model tested

I used a real trigonometric finite-Dirichlet model

\[
F(t)=\sum_{2\le n\le N} n^{-1/2}\cos(\phi_n+t\log n),
\]

where the phases \(\phi_n\) are generated from prime phases:

\[
\phi_n=\sum_{p\le N} v_p(n)\theta_p.
\]

This is more restrictive than giving each \(n\) an independent phase, because composite phases are forced by the prime phases.

I imposed two families of conditions.

First, an off-line-zero equation:

\[
F(-i\eta)=0,
\]

implemented as

\[
\Re F(-i\eta)=0,\qquad \Im F(-i\eta)=0.
\]

Second, finite-jet source flattening of the \(Z_H'''\)-analogue:

\[
F^{(3)}(0)=F^{(4)}(0)=\cdots=F^{(3+R)}(0)=0.
\]

All residuals were normalized by the natural \(\ell^2\) size of the corresponding coefficient vector. I optimized over the prime phases \((\theta_p)\) and \(\eta\).

## Numerical outcomes

The solver found near-exact bad configurations immediately.

| Model | Variables | Constraints | \(\eta\) range | Best normalized residual |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| \(N=50,\ R=6\) | 15 prime phases \(+\eta\) | 9 | \([0.02,1.5]\) | \(7.47\times10^{-11}\) |
| \(N=80,\ R=10\) | 22 prime phases \(+\eta\) | 13 | \([0.02,1.5]\) | \(2.46\times10^{-11}\) |
| \(N=80,\ R=10\) | 22 prime phases \(+\eta\) | 13 | \([0.005,0.2]\) | \(2.90\times10^{-11}\) |
| \(N=100,\ R=10\) | 25 prime phases \(+\eta\) | 13 | \([0.001,0.02]\) | \(1.36\times10^{-11}\) |

The small-\(\eta\) run is the most damaging to the proposed repair. It found

\[
\eta\approx 0.0125
\]

with the off-line-zero equation and jets

\[
F^{(3)}(0),\ldots,F^{(13)}(0)
\]

all essentially zero at normalized residual size \(\sim10^{-11}\).

I also checked the packet energy of \(F'''\) on intervals comparable to the off-line scale. For the small-\(\eta\) solution, the normalized average energy

\[
\frac{\frac1{2H}\int_{-H}^{H}|F'''(t)|^2\,dt}
{\frac12\sum_{n\le N} n^{-1}(\log n)^6}
\]

was about

\[
5.8\times 10^{-25}
\]

for \(H=\eta\), and stayed at that scale for \(H=2\eta\). That is not just pointwise jet cancellation; it gives an actual source-flat packet in the surrogate.

## Interpretation

This is a strong surrogate counterexample to the proposed implication:

\[
\text{off-line zero equation}
+
\text{finite AFE structure}
\Longrightarrow
\text{localized }Z_H''' \text{ mass}.
\]

In the finite-prime phase model, there are many more phase degrees of freedom than constraints. For \(N=80\), there are 22 prime phases plus \(\eta\), while the test imposed only 13 normalized equations. The optimizer finds configurations satisfying both:

\[
F(-i\eta)\approx 0,
\]

and

\[
F^{(3)}(0),\ldots,F^{(13)}(0)\approx0.
\]

This matches the dimension-count concern: finite source-jet nonflatness is not a generic consequence of fixed AFE form. The actual \(\zeta\) trajectory may be more rigid, but that rigidity would need to be a new theorem.

## What this does and does not show

It does **not** prove that actual \(\zeta\) admits such a configuration. The true zeta phases lie on a one-parameter trajectory

\[
t\mapsto (p^{-it})_{p\le N},
\]

and the height \(t=\gamma\) must also be tied to an actual zero. The surrogate allows independent prime phases and then imposes the zero equation. Kronecker-type phase recurrence suggests such finite phase patterns are not obviously forbidden, but that is not the same as producing a zeta zero.

It **does** show that the desired \(Z_H'''\)-entry theorem cannot be proved from:

\[
\text{finite AFE structure},
\quad
\text{zero symmetry},
\quad
\text{mean-square estimates},
\quad
\text{local packet geometry},
\quad
\text{dimension/uncertainty heuristics}.
\]

The theorem would have to be a genuinely new arithmetic nonrecurrence statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual zeta zeros cannot occur at heights where the differentiated Hardy AFE source jets flatten.}
}
\]

That is substantially stronger than anything currently in the draft or agent audits.

## Consequence for the proof strategy

The \(Z_H'''\)-entry repair fast-fails.

The remaining \(Z_H'''\)-based theorem would have to be:

\[
\begin{aligned}
&\text{Let } \rho=\beta+i\gamma,\quad \eta=\left|\beta-\frac12\right|.\\
&\text{For the actual zeta trajectory, if }\zeta(\rho)=0,\text{ then}\\
&\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\partial_t^{3+r}Z_H(m_\rho)
\right|
\ge Q_\rho^{-A},
\end{aligned}
\]

with

\[
Q_\rho=Q(|\gamma|,\eta^{-1},\kappa_\rho^{-1}).
\]

The finite-prime surrogate strongly suggests this is not a natural theorem. It may still be true for actual \(\zeta\), but proving it would require a new, very specific joint zero/source-jet nonrecurrence result.

## Recommendation

Do not continue trying to derive RH-entry from \(Z_H'''\) unless the project is explicitly shifted to proving that new joint nonrecurrence theorem.

The next credible pivot is to replace the RH-entry source with a zero-detecting source: Laguerre, Jensen, or log-curvature of

\[
\Xi(t)=\xi\!\left(\frac12+it\right).
\]

The downstream two-point/four-point and \(K9/Y12\) architecture may still be reusable, but the left-edge source should not be \(Z_H'''\).
